{"uri": "8236524165", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-21", "time": "18:17:38", "dateTime": "2024-07-21T18:17:38Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-21T18:14:28Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7568627595901489, "url": "https://www.si.com/nfl/lions/news/reasons-for-optimism-lions-2024-season", "title": "5 Reasons for Optimism for Lions' 2024 Season", "body": "The Detroit Lions have their eyes on the prize at the start of the 2024 season.\n\nFourth-year coach Dan Campbell has guided the team from the bottom of the NFC North to the top, captivating the national audience and igniting the fan base in the process. Now, the Lions have realistic aspirations of winning the Lombardi Trophy in 2024.\n\nThe Lions' organization has been long associate with losing. In fact, it's no secret that their two playoff wins last season marked the first time the team had won in the postseason in 30 years. Last year's division title also snapped a three-decade span without one.\n\nHowever, the tides are certainly changing in Detroit. Each of the last two Draft classes have been apart of teams that have only finished above .500, and Campbell's record in three seasons is inching ever closer to .500 after a 3-13-1 finish to his first campaign.\n\nThe franchise once synonymous with losing is now changing its tune. With a young group of talent that only knows winning, the culture and expectations are shifting.\n\nAdditionally, Detroit's young nucleus is very talented. Amon-Ra St. Brown and Penei Sewell have already inked massive second contracts, while Aidan Hutchinson may be on the brink. If their rookie seasons are any indication, Jahmyr Gibbs, Sam LaPorta and Brian Branch look like pillars of the future.\n\nHaving just went to the NFC Championship game, the Lions' young collection of talent is building its winning pedigree.\n\nCoaching staff continuity\n\nDetroit has been fortunate to retain the majority of its coaching staff since Campbell took over. Several coaches, such as Ben Johnson, Aaron Glenn, Hank Fraley, Antwaan Randle El and Mark Brunell, have been with the Lions since or before Campbell took over.\n\nAs a result, young players can be treated to familiar schematics year over year. In a league full of turnover and changes, the Lions have been able to retain the coaching talent on their staff.\n\nThat's not to say there hasn't been interest elsewhere, as Johnson and Glenn have both garnered head coaching interest over the last two campaigns. However, both have returned to Detroit with aspirations of leading the organization to a title.\n\nWith Campbell leading the way and so many familiar faces still in tow, Detroit's foundation on the coaching staff remains in solid shape.\n\nImproved secondary\n\nThe Lions' secondary has added several new pieces that are expected to change the fortunes of the unit in 2024. After being one of the NFL's worst pass defenses a year ago, Detroit is relying on players such as Carlton Davis, Terrion Arnold, Amik Robertson and Ennis Rakestraw to compete in a better fashion.\n\nLast year, the cornerback position had the feel of a revolving door of sorts. Detroit struggled to find a second option opposite Cam Sutton, who had struggles of his own. This year, Davis and Arnold are among the possible replacements.\n\nAdditionally, Emmanuel Moseley is back in the fold after an injury cost him most of last season. If he can emerge with a spot, it will be an encouraging sign given the depth that now resides in the cornerback room.\n\nOffensive weapons\n\nThe Lions have a vast array of offensive weapons that allow them to score with any possible opponent. Ben Johnson's offense boasts two talented running backs and a collection of pass-catchers with diverse skill sets.\n\nWith David Montgomery and Jahmyr Gibbs providing a nice 1-2 punch in the run game, Detroit has to worry little about whether or not they can survive on the ground. Gibbs also brings a presence as a pass-catcher that the Lions want to explore more in 2024.\n\nThrough the air, the effort starts and ends with the connection Jared Goff has with Amon-Ra St. Brown. The All-Pro wideout surpassed 1,500 yards last season and looks the part of one of the league's best at his position.\n\nIf Jameson Williams can emerge as a reliable second option, the Lions' offense becomes all the more dangerous. Sam LaPorta offers a secure option at tight end, and Kalif Raymond and Donovan Peoples-Jones will battle for an increased workload at receiver.\n\nToughness in trenches\n\nIt's no secret that the Lions have one of the league's best offensive lines. Sewell and Taylor Decker give the team two solid bookend tackles, and the interior is headlined by one of the NFL's best in Frank Ragnow.\n\nAs a whole, the unit has done an excellent job setting the tone for Detroit's run-oriented scheme. They also have had plenty of success keeping Goff clean in the pocket. Last year, Sewell was one of the best pass-protecting tackles in addition to his prowess as a run-blocker.\n\nDefensively, the Lions have a strong core foundation on the line as well. Aidan Hutchinson will bring the heat as a pass-rusher, and the addition of DJ Reader as the nose tackle could be a game-changer. With Reader occupying the blockers in the middle, players like Alim McNeill could be allowed to roam free or operate with less attention.\n\nBecause the Lions have committed so much to the trenches, they have the ability to dominate the line of scrimmage. By controlling this area of the game, they can put themselves in a position to dominate.", "source": {"uri": "si.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Sports Illustrated"}, "authors": [], "concepts": {"uri": "2024-07-431186941", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "17:17:59", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T17:17:59Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T17:14:47Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7450980544090271, "url": "https://eu.detroitnews.com/story/sports/columnists/bob-wojnowski/2024/07/23/wojo-from-cornfields-to-practice-fields-lions-primed-to-carve-a-new-path/74511339007/", "title": "Wojo: From cornfields to practice fields, Lions primed to carve a new path", "body": "Allen Park -- With the Lions about to open training camp, I'm honored to throw out the first hyperbole. The first of a few, I assume.\n\nHere it is: The Lions' offseason was just as impressive as their postseason. Also, for planning purposes, the Super Bowl is Feb. 9, 2025, in New Orleans.\n\nIf you thought Lions Fervor would abate in the months following their loss to the 49ers in the NFC Championship Game, ha. Have you seen the aerial photo of the gigantic, stunning likeness of Dan Campbell carved into a corn maze in Ingham County? Have you seen the prognostications listing the Lions as a Super Bowl favorite?\n\nIt's not all hyperbole, either. Before their most-anticipated season in perhaps forever, the Lions completed one of their most productive offseasons ever. No contract squabbles, no major personnel losses. They attacked their weaknesses and addressed long-term issues. That doesn't mean they got it all right, but at this stage, we're legally (and logically) required to trust Brad Holmes and Campbell.\n\nThey got their foundational stars signed and aligned, inking Penei Sewell, Amon-Ra St. Brown and Jared Goff to contract extensions totaling approximately $444 million. These weren't signings of desperation, or signs of overreaction. They were strategic moves to confirm a 12-5 season -- plus two playoff victories -- is an expectation, not an anomaly.\n\nIn late April, the Lions welcomed the rest of the NFL to take a look, hosting a wildly successful draft party that set attendance records. Then just for fun, they went ahead and drafted prime prospects at their most vulnerable position, cornerback. We'll see how first-rounder Terrion Arnold and second-rounder Ennis Rakestraw fill out the secondary, but Holmes collected plenty of options, also trading for top cornerback Carlton Davis from Tampa Bay and signing Amik Robertson.\n\nThe Lions weren't compelled to shake up a lineup that came within 30 minutes of reaching the Super Bowl. Most of the 22 offensive and defensive starters are fairly set, and the team even hung onto prized coordinator Ben Johnson, who'd rather operate a top-five offense than lead a bottom-five team elsewhere. Barring injury, the defense (23rd in the league) should be much, much, much (hyperbole!) better.\n\nVegas odds say the Lions have the look of a Super Bowl team. Evaluators say the Lions have top-five talent. Fans say, hey, how about top-two talent?!\n\nThat's the feverish narrative, and also the danger. Campbell knows there's only one more step after the NFC Championship Game, and he embraces the heady expectations. He declared in the spring he wants \"the whole enchilada,\" but with a cautious caveat.\n\n\"I don't care how much better we get or what we add or what we draft -- it's irrelevant,\" he said. \"It's going to be tough. Everybody in our division's going to be loaded back up and you're not hiding from anybody anymore. Everybody's going to want a piece of you.\"\n\nThe good news is, the Lions can counter with as many pieces as virtually anyone, as they officially open camp Wednesday morning. Various websites ranked the top 25 players in the league under 25, and the Lions have five, most of any team, from Jahmyr Gibbs to Sam LaPorta to Aidan Hutchinson to St. Brown to Sewell.\n\nIn three seasons under Holmes and Campbell, the Lions have sharply weighed immediate competitiveness against long-term goals, balanced youth with experience. Their defense was one of the youngest in the league, and it got both younger and more seasoned. Aaron Glenn has a couple more veteran linemen in DJ Reader and Marcus Davenport, which should help the team's second-biggest weakness, the pass rush.\n\nHutchinson has 21 sacks in two seasons and posted a league-high 62 quarterback pressures last year. The pressure for Glenn's defense is to turn those pressures into actual takedowns. One guy who will be watched closely is pass-rush specialist James Houston. He should be healthy after missing nearly the entire season, and if he can reprise his rookie debut in 2022 (eight sacks in seven games), the Lions should boost their sack total (23rd with 41).\n\nExpectations keep growing, and so do the stakes. The team is mulling plans to build a new practice facility, with more seating and access for fans. That's important because the fan base is expanding, and if the franchise asks for more (ticket prices went up an average of 30%), it's imperative to deliver more.\n\nBut beware, the schedule is tougher and the target is larger. The NFC North doesn't look very patsy-ish anymore. Some intrepid experts are picking the Packers to win it, and I'm not revealing their identities to protect them from overly enthusiastic Lions fans.\n\nIt's easy to contemplate big things in the weeks before big things must be delivered, and some tempering might be necessary. I suggested the Lions would go 11-6 and you'd think I called Campbell a vegan who prefers a refreshing seltzer over beer. The Lions are in that sweet spot where the majority of improvement should come from within, rather than purchased in free agency.\n\nSome of the young talent has been revealed, and I think Gibbs is about to become a superstar. But another layer has potential to be tapped, including linebacker Jack Campbell, defensive back Brian Branch and receiver Jameson Williams.\n\nThere is a downside to having abundant talent -- sort of. For now, there don't appear to be any huge roster battles. There's no quarterback controversy, unless you think Hendon Hooker needs to show real progress as the backup. The Lions have a rare situation with two excellent backs, Gibbs and David Montgomery, who complement each other and don't overshadow each other.\n\nAs camp opens, you might have to settle for one fierce starting-job competition, between incumbent kicker Michael Badgley and USFL phenom Jake Bates. That's a spot the Lions could use a leap, perhaps to allow Campbell to opt for a few more 60-yard field goal attempts, and a few less fourth-down passes.\n\nOh, they might gamble slightly less often, but if you think Campbell and the Lions will dramatically alter their identity, you haven't been paying attention. With a 22-8 record since mid-2022, I think we know who the Lions are, and so do they. {"uri": "8239517394", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "13:34:59", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T13:34:59Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T13:34:21Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.729411780834198, "url": "https://www.si.com/nfl/lions/news/what-lions-must-accomplish-training-camp-2024", "title": "8 Things Lions Must Accomplish at Training Camp", "body": "Detroit Lions defensive tackle Brodric Martin. / Junfu Han / USA TODAY NETWORK\n\nThe Detroit Lions are gearing up for what could ultimately be a special 2024 season.\n\nWith the offseason coming to a close, the Lions' roster is making its final preparations for the start of training camp. In the fourth year under Brad Holmes and Dan Campbell, Detroit is in as good a position as any team in the league.\n\nHere are eight things the Lions must accomplish in 2024 in order to have success when the regular season begins in September.\n\nJameson Williams' development\n\nBy letting Josh Reynolds walk, the Lions are setting up an opening for Jameson Williams to step into a bigger role within the offense. The avenue is there for the Alabama product to break out in a big way as the team's second option behind only Amon-Ra St. Brown.\n\nHe showed growth throughout last season, but must now be a consistent option within the offense. Williams dealt with drop issues at the beginning of last year, so consistency will be key. There's no doubting his potential impact with his game-breaking speed, but the next step for him is being a reliable, every down threat within the offense at all levels.\n\nSecondary communication\n\nWith all the new faces in the secondary, Detroit has the look of a much improved defense in 2024. However, the challenge will be getting all the newcomers up to speed in an efficient and timely manner.\n\nCarlton Davis and Amik Robertson are veterans who should have little issue getting up to speed, while rookies Terrion Arnold and Ennis Rakestraw may need more time to develop within the complexities of the scheme.\n\nThe Lions' pass defense was among the team's biggest pitfalls last season, so developing a rapport between the new options will be paramount throughout training camp.\n\nReps for Brodric Martin\n\nAmong the players who are in the biggest need of reps is Brodric Martin, who played in just three games as a rookie last season. The Lions were high on his potential, but he didn't get much in the way of meaningful snaps last season.\n\nThis year, that could change for Martin. He has a valuable opportunity early in camp with DJ Reader placed on the PUP list. As a result, first-team reps are available for the taking at the nose tackle position.\n\nWhile Martin won't need to be an instant game-wrecker, development would be encouraging. He'll likely get plenty of opportunities in the preseason, as well, and could wind up benefiting greatly.\n\nGrowth from Hendon Hooker\n\nAnother player who will get plenty of opportunities this fall is Hendon Hooker. After spending most of last year rehabbing an injury, Hooker will get a chance to go through training camp in full for the first time.\n\nHooker was up-and-down in the spring, and training camp will give him another opportunity to demonstrate his abilities in Ben Johnson's offensive scheme. If he can improve his timing, the Lions' backup quarterback decision becomes much clearer.\n\nNo sophomore slumps\n\nThe Lions had three rookies who were among if not the best at their respective positions in their class. Jahmyr Gibbs, Sam LaPorta and Brian Branch all had fantastic rookie seasons. Now, the key will be maintaining that success and not taking steps back in their second campaigns.\n\nGibbs and LaPorta will be big parts of the offense, while Branch is expected to be a versatile chess piece for the defense. Taking a step forward will be key for each, along with first-round pick Jack Campbell.\n\nAfter taking his lumps as a rookie, Campbell appears primed for a bigger role in 2024. If he can take the next step, Detroit's 2023 Draft class could be among the best in recent memory.\n\nOverall health\n\nBranch was among four players that the Lions placed on injury lists ahead of the start of training camp. While injuries are a natural part of the game, remaining healthy will be exceptionally important for the Lions during camp.\n\nThe current injuries will give the Lions opportunities to evaluate their depth. However, having their key pieces ready to go for the start of training camp will be pivotal. Whether it's being patient with current injured players or monitoring workloads, Detroit must put itself in position to field their best lineups when the regular season approaches.\n\nKicker stability\n\nThe Lions have struggled to find kicker stability since Matt Prater departed after the 2020 season. Now, perhaps the biggest competition at the position of Campbell's tenure looms in camp.\n\nThe incumbent, Michael Badgley, is a player whom the staff is fond of and has been solid during his two years with the Lions. However, he'll battle UFL sensation Jake Bates for the job.\n\nBates has immense popularity with the Lions' fan base after nailing several long-range kicks with the Michigan Panthers this spring. Detroit needs stability at the position, as it's one that can win or lose big games.\n\nHandling expectations\n\nMore than anything, the Lions must manage the big expectations facing them in 2024. After years of being an afterthought, the organization is being placed among the league's elite by pundits. It would be little surprise if the team was in contention for a title at the end of the regular season.\n\nGetting back to where they finished last season and clearing that final hurdle will be no easy task, however. As a result, the overall attitude of the team and morale throughout camp will be closely monitored.\n\nHolmes and Campbell have worked diligently to construct a championship-caliber roster. {"uri": "8237695988", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-22", "time": "12:41:56", "dateTime": "2024-07-22T12:41:56Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-22T12:41:06Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7176470756530762, "url": "https://www.si.com/nfl/lions/news/lions-2024-training-camp-primer", "title": "Detroit Lions 2024 Training Camp Primer", "body": "Detroit Lions defensive end Aidan Hutchinson (97). / Junfu Han / USA TODAY NETWORK\n\nFourth-year coach Dan Campbell put it plainly during the spring, saying he wants, \"the whole enchilada,\" in the form of a Super Bowl championship. The Lions proved they belong among the league's best with their run to the NFC Championship last season, and are hoping to exceed that mark this year.\n\nThe road won't be easy, but Campbell and Brad Holmes have put together a strong infrastructure for the future. The Super Bowl window is open, and the time is now for the Lions to take advantage.\n\nHere is a recap of the offseason, as well as a preview of what's to come in 2024 as the Lions get set to beginning training camp this week.\n\nKey losses\n\nThe Lions lost two starters on the offensive side of the ball in free agency. Offensive guard Jonah Jackson departed for a three-year deal with the Los Angeles Rams, while wide receiver Josh Reynolds inked a two-year agreement with the Denver Broncos.\n\nJackson was a starter for the duration of his four years with the Lions but struggled with injuries in the final year of his rookie deal. Reynolds, meanwhile, was a strong downfield threat who had good rapport with Jared Goff dating back to their time together with the Los Angeles Rams.\n\nDefensively, the Lions will be without two of their higher profile free agency additions from a season ago. C.J. Gardner-Johnson returned to the Philadelphia Eagles after injuries sidelined him for a majority of last year, while Cam Sutton was released after a legal issue and ultimately returned to the Pittsburgh Steelers.\n\nBoth players were expected to be big additions for the secondary, but neither panned out. Gardner-Johnson missed 14 regular season games with a torn pec, while Sutton struggled to lock down opposing top wide receivers.\n\nTracy Walker III was released in the offseason and has yet to find a new team, while Jerry Jacobs was not retained as a restricted free agent after starting 12 games last season at cornerback.\n\nOther depth departures include offensive linemen Matt Nelson and Halapoulivaati Vaitai and defensive end Charles Harris. Backup quarterback Teddy Bridgewater and defensive lineman Romeo Okwara both retired from the NFL.\n\nKey additions\n\nThe secondary was the biggest target area of the Lions this offseason, as Holmes devoted several resources to adding better talent to the group. Detroit acquired Carlton Davis in a trade on the first day of the legal tampering period and signed fellow cornerback Amik Robertson the following day.\n\nHolmes also addressed the defensive line, adding a pair of high-upside pieces. DJ Reader has been one of the NFL's better nose tackles, and Marcus Davenport has strong potential despite injuries limiting his progress throughout his career.\n\nTo fill the void left by Jackson at the guard position, the Lions inked a one-year deal with veteran guard Kevin Zeitler. The 12-year veteran has played for four NFL teams previously and has been one of the league's most durable linemen.\n\nWith all the newcomers, the Lions will have options at the cornerback position. Davis appears primed to be the top option, but there will be a battle for the starting spot opposite him. Arnold is a popular pick, but adjusting to life as a corner at the NFL level can be difficult.\n\nIf Arnold can't claim the second spot, Robertson could be a natural fit. Though undersized, Robertson plays with an edge and has versatility to play either on the boundary or in the slot as the nickel cornerback. Rakestraw can also stake his claim at the role with a strong spring.\n\nAnother intriguing option is Emmanuel Moseley. After coming to Detroit on a one-year deal last season, Moseley played in just one game before suffering a season-ending knee injury. The Lions like his potential enough to give him another opportunity, and he appears to be close to healthy as camp begins.\n\nDefensive end\n\nAidan Hutchinson took another big step forward in his second NFL season, and looks the part of one of the league's best young pass-rushers. However, the Lions' pass-rush struggled overall and finished near the bottom of the league in sacks.\n\nAs a result, one of the more intriguing storylines will center on who emerges as the team's second option in this area. James Houston is a trendy pick after injuries cut his campaign short last year, as he burst onto the scene as a rookie and showed flashes of dominance.\n\nDavenport is another option if he can remain healthy, though he will start training camp on the PUP list. John Cominsky has been a stable veteran presence, but will need an uptick in production to warrant serious consideration.\n\nFormer CFL standout Mathieu Betts is a dark horse option, as he was a force at that level working off the edge. If Betts can emerge into a standout, his signing will be considered one of Holmes' most shrewd moves.\n\nWide receiver\n\nThere's no question that Amon-Ra St. Brown is the team's top option at wideout, and a path has been set for Jameson Williams to emerge as the second. However, there's a battle expected for the third wideout option after Reynolds' departure.\n\nKalif Raymond appears to be the leader in the clubhouse as it stands, but Donovan Peoples-Jones and Antoine Green are ready for roles bigger than what they had with the team a year ago.\n\nAdditionally, unheralded options such as Daurice Fountain and Kaden Davis could give the Lions interesting decisions after strong showings in spring workouts.\n\nLinebacker\n\nEvery indication shows that Jack Campbell is ready for a bigger role in 2024 after an up-and-down rookie year, but last season showed that nothing is guaranteed. After all, Campbell was beaten out for a starting spot by Derrick Barnes after being drafted 18th overall last year.\n\nCampbell was praised for his offseason efforts and is emerging as a leader, so there's plenty to like about his trajectory. Barnes won't go quietly, though, and Malcolm Rodriguez could also factor in after taking on a smaller role last year.\n\nKicker\n\nThe Lions have a serious kicking competition after the addition of Jake Bates. The UFL standout and viral sensation has a big leg, but consistency will be key for him to beat out the incumbent Michael Badgley.\n\nThough not posting flashy long-range kicks, Badgley has been consistent through parts of two seasons with the organization. He lost out on the job last year during the spring, but was brought back on the practice squad and eventually beat out Riley Patterson to win the job late in the year.\n\nThere are high expectations for Bates given his success at the UFL level. {"uri": "8238087630", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-22", "time": "17:12:14", "dateTime": "2024-07-22T17:12:14Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-22T17:11:17Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7176470756530762, "url": "https://www.si.com/nfl/lions/news/reasons-for-worry-lions-2024-season", "title": "5 Reasons for Worry Ahead of Lions' 2024 Season", "body": "Getting back to the stage where the 2023 season ended will be a difficult task for the Detroit Lions.\n\nDan Campbell, the team's fourth-year coach, said as much in the immediate aftermath of the NFC Championship loss to the San Francisco 49ers. The leader admitted that getting back to that point in the season will be twice as hard as it was in 2023.\n\nStill, Detroit believes it has the necessary pieces in place to be among the league's best in 2024. With training camp set to begin this week, plenty will be learned about Detroit and where it stands after this month.\n\nHere are five reasons for concern ahead of the 2024 season.\n\nNFC North improvements\n\nThe Lions won the NFC North for the first time in franchise history last season and are looking to repeat with many of their core pieces still in place. While the title was rightfully earned, the Lions will face a tougher challenge within the division in 2024.\n\nEach of the opposing teams seem to be improved from where they finished the 2023 campaign. For starters, Green Bay nearly upended the 49ers in the Divisional Round and beat the Lions in their second matchup last season.\n\nWith Jordan Love playing at such a high level, the Packers seem to have their quarterback of the future in place. Green Bay added defensive playmakers as well as running back Josh Jacobs.\n\nChicago drafted Caleb Williams as well as Rome Odunze, setting up an offense that threatens to be much improved from a year ago. Minnesota faltered last year after Kirk Cousins' injury and still has questions under center, but the Vikings should be improved from where they finished last season.\n\nBecause each of the teams in the North got better, the Lions will face a gauntlet within the division. Last season proved that there were no cakewalks to begin with, but this season could see the NFC North be one of the best divisions in the league.\n\nDifficult schedule\n\nBecause the Lions finished first in their division, they will play top teams in other divisions. The Lions will play eight games against teams that made the playoffs last year, including rematches with each of their three postseason opponents.\n\nDetroit opens the year with games against the Rams and Buccaneers, both of whom will be looking for revenge after the Lions ended their seasons in the playoffs. Also mixed in the schedule will be a showdown with Buffalo and road games at Dallas and Houston.\n\nThe Lions will certainly be battle tested as a result, with tough opponents and environments littered throughout the schedule.\n\nPass defense concerns\n\nThe Lions' pass defense was one of the league's worst last year for multiple reasons. It was a struggle in the secondary, while the pass-rush also struggled to generate heat.\n\nWith offseason moves, Detroit hopes it has pulled the necessary strings in both areas. Carlton Davis and Terrion Arnold are expected to help the secondary, while Marcus Davenport could be a difference maker in the pass-rush.\n\nDetroit's defense finished second in the league against the run last season, so the efforts in that area were exemplary. However, they will need an uptick in production against the pass if they are to eventually reach their lofty goals.\n\nHistory's trends\n\nHistorically, it has been tough for teams to reach the Super Bowl the year after losing in the NFC Championship game. The 49ers did it last year, becoming the first team to do so since they did it under Jim Harbaugh in the 2011 season.\n\nAs a result, history is not on the side of the Lions' success in 2024. Detroit is facing more buzz than ever before, and as a result will face pressure to live up to the high expectations.\n\nInjury threats\n\nIf there's one factor that can quickly derail a team, it's the injury bug. The Lions were fortunate to remain mostly healthy throughout last season, a luxury not afforded to every team given the physical nature of the game.\n\nThe Lions will start training camp with four players on injury lists, including a pair of key free agent additions in Marcus Davenport and DJ Reader. Both players have injury history, so monitoring their health will be key.\n\nAnother area that has been impacted by injuries in recent years is the offensive line. Frank Ragnow dealt with a myriad amount of bumps and bruises last season. Teams in recent years with Super Bowl aspirations have had their seasons derailed by injuries, so having reliable depth in place will be just as important as keeping the starters healthy.", "source": {"uri": "8239076065", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "09:05:36", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T09:05:36Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T09:04:41Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6980392336845398, "url": "https://www.nytimes.com/athletic/5651631/2024/07/23/detroit-lions-training-camp-storylines-players-to-watch-rookies/", "title": "Lions training camp: Storylines, players to watch, position battles and more", "body": "Since their arrival some three and a half years ago, everything Dan Campbell and Brad Holmes have been building has been to get to this point, right here, right now.\n\nThey have proof of concept, with a team that not only lived up to lofty expectations set a year ago, but far exceeded them. They have coaches who've been courted by other teams, only to remain in Detroit to see this through. They have a roster full of young, dynamic talent -- among the NFL's best. They've supplemented that core with veterans hungry to win and win for this city after tasting success in January.\n\nThese Detroit Lions, on paper, have everything needed to win a Super Bowl. Not often you can say that about this franchise.\n\nBut that's where we are. And the road to New Orleans begins this week, as training camp kicks off in Allen Park, Mich.\n\nOftentimes, success in this league isn't linear. It's what makes what the Lions have done so impressive. Each year of the Dan Campbell era, the Lions have shown noticeable improvement. From 3-13-1 to 9-8 to 12-5 and a trip to the NFC Championship game, it's been a steady yet remarkable rise for a franchise that's been anything but over the years. It's a testament to Sheila Hamp, Chris Speilman, Campbell, Holmes and company for getting the organization this far, but the work isn't done. The goal for these Lions now is clear. It starts with a division title, which could prove more difficult than last year with the Packers looking like a threat and the Bears on the rise. They should be aiming for the No. 1 seed in the NFC. And if all goes according to plan, Campbell will be eating enchiladas in February.\n\nHow will the Lions handle the target on their backs?\n\nEven though the Lions were NFC North favorites entering the 2023 season, they hadn't accomplished anything yet. Division title bragging rights belonged to Minnesota, and the Lions hadn't hung a banner for winning one in 30 years. Of course, that all changed last season, which now elevates the Lions as the team to beat. While the team did well to turn a good roster into a strong one, they'll now face a first-place schedule and what's looking like a tougher division. The Packers nearly took down the 49ers to reach the NFC Championship, and they remain one of the league's youngest rosters. The Bears have a rising defense and an offense that added No. 1 pick Caleb Williams, No. 9 pick Rome Odunze, star WR Keenan Allen and RB D'Andre Swift. Even the Vikings remained competitive without Kirk Cousins last year. The NFC North is coming for the Lions. They'll need to be ready.\n\nIs this the last dance for Campbell's closest confidants?\n\nFor years, we've been wondering when Lions offensive coordinator Ben Johnson and defensive coordinator Aaron Glenn might leave Detroit. And for years, they've remained in their positions as OC and DC. It's rare to have this kind of continuity in the NFL. It wouldn't be surprising to see Campbell's coordinators remain in Detroit -- they like it here, after all. However, it does feel like a matter of time before the band breaks up. Things could look different a year from now, and if that's what's in store, it makes winning this year, with a team that has what it takes to do it, all the more important.\n\nIs the new-look secondary enough to propel the defense?\n\nWhen you have a team that makes it within a game of the Super Bowl and returns its core roster, you don't have to reinvent the wheel. The offense should remain one of the best in the league with Goff and Johnson running it. But what about the defense? Glenn's group improved in some areas -- most notably, a run defense that ranked 2nd in the league in yards per game allowed -- but the passing defense was very much a liability, both in the regular season and the playoffs. Some new faces could help Glenn return to the man-heavy defense he wants to play, but we need to see results.\n\nWR Jameson Williams: You can't talk players to watch without talking Jameson Williams. Stepping into a larger role in 2024, this is his most important season yet. In terms of pure fit, Williams is everything the Lions need in this offense. He's the perfect complement to Amon-Ra St. Brown and Sam LaPorta in the passing game, as his deep-threat ability can open up the underneath game for others, and vice versa. The spring showed a more focused Williams, working with the first-team offense. We'll see what training camp has in store.\n\nQB Hendon Hooker: Jared Goff has been durable in his Lions' tenure, but these are things you have to think about when you reach contender status. The Lions will need to have a capable backup in the event Goff goes down for a bit, and they're turning to Hooker -- a 2023 third-round pick -- to fill that role. Hooker has natural skill and maturity beyond his years, but he faced growing pains this offseason as he corrected his footwork. The hope is that he'll look smoother in August, but we won't know until the preseason games begin.\n\nLB Jack Campbell: The No. 18 pick in the 2023 draft, Campbell didn't have the same immediate success as other rookies in the class. However, coaches have raved about his offseason. He's been deemed a \"grown man\" for the way he controls the huddle. This will be his first full season as a green-dot Mike linebacker, and if he can take a leap forward, this defense will follow.\n\nDB Brian Branch: It only took a year, but Branch is one of the Lions' most valuable defenders. And while he settled in nicely at nickel a year ago, there's a chance he plays safety more regularly in 2024. Just how much remains to be seen, but wherever he spends the majority of his time will have ripple effects on the rest of the secondary.\n\nCB Terrion Arnold: The Lions trading up to pick No. 24 for Arnold felt inevitable the longer the first round played out. He's a perfect fit in terms of everything the Lions look for out of their corners -- a competitive mindset, confidence and the ability to play man coverage. It might take time for him to get there, but he's the best CB prospect they've added since Holmes and Campbell arrived. He'll compete for a starting gig.\n\nCB Ennis Rakestraw Jr.: If Arnold is No. 1 CB prospect, Rakestraw is right there as the No. 2. In fact, Rakestraw was the second-highest-ranked corner on the team's board behind Arnold this past April. They're different personalities -- Arnold is flashier, while Rakestraw is a bit more reserved -- but they're both alphas on the field. Detroit's front office was shocked Rakestraw was still available at No. 61 and even considered trading up for him. That should tell you what they think of him. Rakestraw was spotted playing nickel in the spring, which might be his fastest path to playing time -- even if he's not a regular starter.\n\nOL Giovanni Manu: This is very much a development year for Manu. He's got tools for days -- size, length, mobility, power -- but he'll have to learn how to hone it in the NFL. The Lions traded a 2025 third-round pick to get into the fourth round for Manu, a sign that they believe in his upside. The plan is to cross train Manu at tackle and guard, and let him sit behind one of the league's best offensive lines. With that in mind, expectations should be minimal for Year 1, and most likely, Year 2 as well. He needs time.\n\nRB Sione Vaki: If you followed Vaki's story before the draft, you couldn't help but feel like he was a fit for the Lions. A hardworking athlete who played safety or running back in college and could do the same in the NFL, the Lions will start Vaki off at running back and see how he develops. After watching him in OTAs, it feels like the right move. He's a natural with the ball in his hands and his film as a rusher in college showed a player who doesn't go down on first contact. There's real value in that for a team that runs the ball as much as the Lions do, and he can also be a weapon on special teams. Fun one to watch.\n\nDL Mekhi Wingo: A sixth-round pick out of LSU, Wingo was thought of by a few draft experts as a potential top-100 talent. He comes in a smaller frame (6-foot, 291 pounds), but he adds some pass-rush juice from the interior. The Lions believe he can play on the edge, too. Don't be surprised if he works his way into the playing rotation early on.\n\nOG Christian Mahogany: Another sixth-rounder given a fourth-round grade by many during the pre-draft process, Mahogany looks like a pro. He's got four years of starting experience under his belt from Boston College. He's competitive and has a mean streak in his game. His favorite player growing up was Larry Allen and wears No. 73 because of it. He just feels like a guy who'll wind up starting for 10 seasons.\n\nWR3: We know St. Brown and Williams will start, but who might join them? The early favorites are Donovan Peoples-Jones and Antoine Green, and if the Lions don't add a veteran here before camp is over, it's because they're confident in one of these two stepping in. Kalif Raymond could also see an uptick in usage to account for the loss of Josh Reynolds. Perhaps Jahmyr Gibbs, too.\n\nEdge: The Lions felt they needed more along the edge, so they added a familiar face in Marcus Davenport. Campbell and Glenn know Davenport from their days in New Orleans, but it's been that long since he was a standout. His breakout 2021 campaign helped put him on the map, but he hasn't been able to recreate that magic since -- with injuries plaguing him. If he's healthy, he's most likely your starter opposite Aidan Hutchinson, but don't count out a third-year Josh Paschal.\n\nSecondary: There could be some moving parts in the secondary, so it's worth talking about the backend all together. Carlton Davis III has a starting spot locked up at outside corner, but there's competition elsewhere. If Branch remains at nickel full-time, you'll see a competition between Arnold and free-agent addition Amik Robertson for the spot next to Davis. Perhaps Rakestraw for Emmanuel Moseley, coming off a torn ACL, joins the action as well. But right now, it feels like Arnold vs. Robertson.\n\nIf Branch moves to safety on a more regular basis, the nickel spot suddenly becomes open. In that event, Robertson would be the clear frontrunner for the position, with Rakestraw perhaps factoring in down the road if Robertson struggles. In this scenario, you'd likely see Arnold and Davis on the outside, Robertson at nickel and Branch at one safety spot. Kerby Joseph and Ifeatu Melifonwu are two starting-caliber safeties in the NFL, but one would have to move to the bench. The Lions value Joseph's ballhawk skills as a centerfielder in this defense, so the early nod goes to him.\n\nKicker: Another year, another kicking competition in Detroit. This is the most anticipated one by far, though. Michael Badgley is the incumbent, and a player who's been with the organization since 2022. He'll face Jake Bates -- a fan favorite from his time with the UFL Michigan Panthers with range from 60-plus. You made it. Football officially returns with the start of training camp this week.\n\nThe Detroit Lions will begin their quest to appear in Super Bowl LIX in practice this week, and in the meantime, we've got a couple key position battles for you to watch this summer.\n\nCornerback\n\nWe'll start with the obvious. Most of the top players on Detroit's cornerback depth chart are newcomers: Carlton Davis III (via trade), Terrion Arnold (draft), Ennis Rakestraw (draft) and Amik Robertson (free agency). Even Emmanuel Moseley, who signed with Detroit in the 2023 offseason, is basically a new body, after not returning until Week 4 and getting injured on his second play.\n\nGiven the third-round pick Detroit used to acquire Davis, plus his time on task in the league, it can be safely assumed he's CB1. But outside of that? All bets are off.\n\nThe intrigue comes in tandem with Detroit's safety situation. The Lions will probably want Ifeatu Melifonwu and Kerby Joseph on the field a ton next year, but depending on how they use Brian Branch -- who they believe can be a guy that plays darn near every position, including high safety -- there might be more snaps available at nickel corner than one might think.\n\nRobertson, Arnold and Rakestraw all have experience in the slot, but each man would likely prefer to play outside.\n\nAt the bottom of the depth chart, expect it to be an intense battle between Khalil Dorsey, Steven Gilmore, Kindle Vildor and Morice Norris.\n\nLinebacker\n\nDerrick Barnes somewhat defied expectations last season by earning his role as the team's No. 2 off-ball linebacker next to Alex Anzalone, but everything we've heard from the coaching staff seems to indicate that Jack Campbell, the 2023 first-rounder, is coming.\n\nIt remains to be seen what that means for Barnes, but the Lions did a good job last season of using every member of their linebacking unit -- perhaps the most underrated on the roster -- in a way that played to their strengths. Heck, Malcolm Rodriguez was catching passes in 2023 while Jalen Reeves-Maybin made second-team AP All-Pro for his role on special teams. Anzalone will be a leader of the defense once again, but behind him, there's a lot that needs to be figured out between now and Week 1 -- and that's by no means a bad thing.\n\nDefensive line\n\nOutside of Aidan Hutchinson, Alim McNeill and DJ Reader, it feels as though every spot on the defensive line is up for grabs -- and that's if the 30-year-old Reader has fully recovered his second torn quad in four seasons.\n\nIf he can stay healthy, veteran free-agent signing Marcus Davenport feels like he'll be in pole position to be Hutchinson's main running partner on the edge. But there's also reason to believe this could be Josh Paschal's breakout year; John Cominsky won't go away quietly and there's a good amount of intrigue on what Mathieu Betts, the CFL Defensive Player of the Year, can bring to the table.\n\nLast season, many thought James Houston would be the team's other starting defensive end, but the Lions seemed committed to rounding him into a true outside linebacker -- and then he suffered an ankle injury in Week 2 that was just about season-ending, save a couple of snaps in the playoffs. His deployment will be among the biggest things to watch in camp.\n\nOn the interior, Reader's injury could open the door for others to announce themselves as next. It should be fun to see who emerges from a young group of recent draft picks that includes Levi Onwuzurike, Brodric Martin and Mekhi Wingo while Chris Smith and Kyle Peko fight for their spots.\n\nWide receiver\n\nAfter losing Josh Reynolds to free agency, many considered receiver to be a (minor) position of need for the Lions entering this offseason. It appears the Lions' brass did not agree; they didn't add anybody of note. The Lions carried five receivers into the regular season last year, and we can safely assume that Amon-Ra St. Brown, Jameson Williams and Kalif Raymond will account for three of those spots in 2024.\n\nDonovan Peoples-Jones also seems a front-runner to be an impact player and fill the Reynolds role. Though he didn't have much involvement after being dealt to Detroit at the deadline last season, he did catch seven of the eight passes thrown his way and produced 839 receiving yards just two seasons ago.\n\nIf we assume that experience wins out and the Lions only carry five receivers once again, that leaves just one roster spot between Antoine Green, Tre'Quan Smith, Maurice Alexander, Tom Kennedy, Daurice Fountain, Tre'Quan Smith and a few other youngsters. Of that group, only Green has the luxury of being a Brad Holmes pick -- which, historically, bodes well for sticking around. But the Lions have carried both Alexander and Kennedy for a handful of years, so maybe one of them gets a crack at the initial 53 if Green fails to impress.\n\nTight end\n\nThe Lions have their top two tight-end spots locked down with Sam LaPorta and Brock Wright. The battle for TE3 will likely come down to James Mitchell, who's entering year three, and Shane Zylstra, who's coming off a season-ending knee injury that he suffered in training camp last year.\n\nTight ends coach Steve Heiden has been complimentary of the way Mitchell ended last season (his first healthy season in the league), and, as previously mentioned, the Lions typically like to see their draft picks through.\n\nLike running back, the Lions carried three tight ends into last season but have carried four before, and perhaps this is where the Lions get their \"fullback\" from, with Jason Cabinda still a free agent. Three years later, they were 30 minutes of football away from the Super Bowl and have exceeded expectations -- even if they're reluctant to take the credit.\n\n\"I remember when we first got here, everybody was wondering kind of how long this was going to take, how long is this build going to be,\" Holmes reflected after the 2023 season. \"And I remember I used the word 'retool' and I got killed because I probably should've used the word rebuild. [...] I never wanted to put a timestamp on it -- or an anchor -- a time anchor on it because I said, 'Look, we're just going to do our job, roll our sleeves up, and work to improve every single day.' And that's what we did. So, it's hard for me to say, 'Yeah, we are ahead of schedule.' Because I don't know what that original timestamp should've been in the first place. But I do know we love where we are at and I believe we are at where exactly where we're supposed to be.\"\n\nA big key to their success in 2023 was the return of a top-five offense, paired with an elite run defense, which kept them in position to win games in ways that had previously eluded their reach. But as impressive as their defensive growth was, they still had glaring weaknesses in their secondary, and teams routinely took advantage.\n\nWith overhauling the secondary at the forefront of Detroit's agenda this offseason, Holmes attacked the problem in a variety of ways during the 2024 offseason.\n\nThe first step in upgrading the Lions' secondary began by moving on from both starting outside corners, releasing Cam Sutton after a domestic battery by strangulation arrest and allowing Jerry Jacobs to depart after his contract expired. They also allowed C.J. Gardner-Johnson and Tracy Walker -- both briefly held starting jobs in 2023 -- to exit Detroit this offseason.\n\nTo replace their corners, Holmes traded for veteran Carlton Davis and signed veteran Amik Robertson in free agency. In the NFL Draft. The Lions used their first and second-round picks on cornerbacks, trading up and selecting Terrion Arnold with pick No. 24, then snagging Ennis Rakestraw with pick No. 61 overall. They also re-signed Emmanuel Moseley to a one-year deal, hoping he could return to the starter competition after tearing his ACL for the second consecutive season. The Lions are counting on their new additions to create a five-way competition for starting jobs that will result in a higher level of play on the outside.\n\nBrian Branch returns as the Lions' primary option in the slot, while Kerby Joseph and Ifeatu Melifonwu maintain their starting safety roles. The Lions did little to replace Gardner-Johnson and Walker, only re-signing special teams ace C.J. Moore (after he served his year-long suspension for gambling), but are planning on expanding Branch's role to include more reps at safety.\n\n\"We have so many options right now, so much competitiveness,\" Campbell said during minicamp. \"[Lions defensive coordinator Aaron Glenn] AG and I were talking about it again, and Brad and I talk about it every evening: the talent level, the competitiveness, the versatility. Honestly, we have no idea who our starting lineups are going to be right now and it's exciting.\"\n\nAs exciting as it may be for Campbell to have new players to work with, in order for the Lions to have success, they'll need several things to happen through training camp and the preseason. Newly-acquired veterans will need to adjust to the Lions' scheme, rookies will need to adapt to the talent level of the NFL, injured players will need to prove they're healthy, and returning players need to expand their roles while maintaining or exceeding their level of play. Additionally, with the number of new players competing for starting jobs, and because communication is paramount in the Lions' split-zone scheme, establishing a report quickly will be vital to early season success.\n\nIn the first two weeks of the season, the Lions face the Los Angeles Rams and Tampa Bay Buccaneers, two teams they faced in the playoffs last season that will be difficult early tests. If the Lions' secondary is not on point from the jump, both offenses have shown that they have the potential to score points in Ford Field. If the Lions hope to match or exceed their 12-5 record from last season, the opening two games will be critical to that process.\n\nOn paper, the Lions' offseason aggression looks to be an upgrade to The franchise has taken the necessary approach to accomplish that task by locking down its foundational players in QB Jared Goff, WR Amon-Ra St. Brown and OT Penei Sewell with massive offseason extensions, while revamping its secondary with new faces such as rookie DBs Terrion Arnold and Ennis Rakestraw Jr.\n\nThe Lions were able to snap some notable droughts in 2023 with their first division title since 1993 as well as their first playoff victory and conference championship appearance since 1991 and will enter this season with high expectations.\n\n\"If I had to put it in one word, I would just say contender. I know it's gonna be very hard, if not harder, than it was last year because people might do a little extra homework when they're playing us, but just knowing the character of our locker room, that's just what we, as a team, want to be about,\" Lions veteran offensive tackle Taylor Decker told ESPN. \"And if you're not trying to compete for championships, much like me taking pride in what I do, it's like, 'What are we doing here?' This is all about winning.\"\n\nHere is a 53-man roster projection as the Lions open training camp.\n\nQUARTERBACKS (2): Jared Goff, Hendon Hooker\n\nGoff has established himself as the clear-cut guy, agreeing to a four-year, $212 million contract extension during the offseason. The 2016 No. 1 pick completed 407 passes last season, which were the second most in the NFL and the most by a Lions QB since Matthew Stafford in 2012. Detroit will also continue to develop Hooker as a backup.\n\nRUNNING BACKS (4): David Montgomery, Jahmyr Gibbs, Craig Reynolds, Sione Vaki\n\nGibbs and Montgomery formed one of the most potent tandems in the league. Montgomery rushed for 1,015 yards in 2023, while Gibbs finished 55 yards shy of 1,000 but had 37 fewer carries than his counterpart. The last team with a pair of running backs with 1,000 rushing yards in a single season was the 2009 Panthers with Jonathan Stewart and DeAngelo Williams. The Lions have a legitimate chance to be the next, barring injuries.\n\nWIDE RECEIVERS (5): Amon-Ra St. Brown, Donovan Peoples-Jones, Jameson Williams, Antoine Green, Kalif Raymond\n\nSt. Brown had nine games with 100-plus receiving yards last season, most in the NFL and most by a Lions receiver since Hall of Famer Calvin Johnson's franchise-record 12 in 2012. He is motivated to reach new heights after agreeing to a four-year, $120 million extension in the offseason. The Lions are looking for third-year receiver Williams to take a leap and help the offense reach a new level after showing flashes of his playmaking ability last season.\n\nTIGHT ENDS (3): Sam LaPorta, Brock Wright, Shane Zylstra\n\nLaPorta experienced one of the greatest rookie seasons by a tight end in league history. He was one of seven Lions players to earn Pro Bowl honors while being named a finalist for the 2023 Offensive Rookie of the Year. LaPorta had at least five receptions in 10 games, most among rookie tight ends in NFL history. He finished with 86 receptions for 889 yards and 10 touchdowns, all franchise records for a tight end.\n\nOFFENSIVE LINEMEN (9): Taylor Decker, Graham Glasgow, Frank Ragnow, Kevin Zeitler, Penei Sewell, Colby Sorsdal, Dan Skipper, Giovanni Manu, Christian Mahogany\n\nSewell has established himself as one of the brightest stars in the league after a first-team All-Pro season. The seventh overall pick in 2021 signed an extension that'll lock him down in Detroit through the 2029 season. Detroit also added Pro Bowl guard Zeitler after losing Jonah Jackson to the Los Angeles Rams via free agency.\n\nDEFENSIVE LINEMEN (10): Aidan Hutchinson, Alim McNeill, DJ Reader, Marcus Davenport, Levi Onwuzurike, John Cominsky, Brodric Martin, Mekhi Wingo, Josh Paschal, Mathieu Betts\n\nThe defensive line needs a boost. The Lions ranked 27th in the NFL and last among playoff teams in pass rush win rate at 35.8%. Their run stop win rate by interior lineman was 27.4%, which was the second worst in the league, ahead of only the Chiefs. Detroit added former Bengals defensive tackle Reader to help.\n\nLINEBACKERS (6): Jack Campbell, Alex Anzalone, Derrick Barnes, Jalen Reeves-Maybin, James Houston, Ben Niemann\n\nSelected 18th overall in the 2023 NFL draft, Campbell will look to take a leap in Year 2. He didn't have the greatest statistical season as a rookie but did make an impact, with 95 total tackles and a pair of sacks. The competition will be strong within this unit during training camp.\n\nCORNERBACKS (7): Carlton Davis III, Emmanuel Moseley, Steven Gilmore, Terrion Arnold, Amik Robertson, Ennis Rakestraw Jr., Khalil Dorsey\n\nThe Lions took an aggressive approach in upgrading the secondary, which was one of the squad's weakest units in 2023. They struggled when the ball was in the air, allowing 34 receptions thrown 20-plus yards downfield, which tied for the second-most in the NFL. Detroit is hoping that top pick Arnold can help plug those holes. The 24th overall selection had five interceptions and 12 pass breakups with Alabama in 2023, which both tied for the most in the SEC.\n\nSAFETIES (4): Brian Branch, Kerby Joseph, Ifeatu Melifonwu, C.J. Moore\n\nThe Lions are expecting to get Branch back for training camp after the second-year defensive back missed minicamp and most of the organized team activities after undergoing surgery on his lower left leg. Branch was spotted in a walking boot while using a scooter over the summer after a strong first season in which he ranked second among all rookies with three interceptions.\n\nSPECIALISTS (3): Jake Bates, Jack Fox, Scott Daly\n\nBates made the 2024 All-UFL Team with the Michigan Panthers. He holds the record for the second-longest field goal in pro football history with a 64-yard game-winning kick in the season opener against the St. Louis Battlehawks, which was just two yards less They had also never won the NFC North division, logging their last division title in the defunct NFC Central. If you asked just about any Lions fan before the 2023 season if they'd be pleased with one playoff victory and an NFC North title, they would say yes in a heartbeat.\n\nInstead, the Lions won two playoff games and came one horrible half of football away from appearing in their first Super Bowl.\n\nNow Detroit is expected to repeat as a Super Bowl contender in the NFC in 2024. If they want that to happen, they'll need a few things to break their way this season.\n\nOne of those is improved play from their defense. Detroit's pass defense was one of the worst in the NFL, and it was one of the big factors that cost them a trip to the Super Bowl. The Lions allowed the most passing plays of 20+ yards in the NFL last season and were in the bottom half of the league in most statistical categories related to defending the pass. Thankfully, GM Brad Holmes has invested heavily in remaking the team's cornerback room. Detroit added Carlton Davis III, Amik Robertson, Terrion Arnold, and Ennis Rakestraw Jr. via free agency and the 2024 NFL Draft. There is no doubt this unit will be improved in 2024.\n\nThe Lions need Jameson Williams to take a huge leap forward in 2024. Will he deliver?\n\nThe Lions also need to replace Josh Reynolds' production on offense. Reynolds had great chemistry from his time with Goff in Los Angeles and was an important part of the passing game. In 2023, Reynolds logged 40 receptions for 608 yards and five touchdowns. He was third on the team in receiving yards behind only Amon-Ra St. Brown and Sam LaPorta.\n\nIf Detroit wants to stay on top of the NFC, they'll need to replace Reynolds in the aggregate.\n\nDan Campbell and the Lions are counting on Jameson Williams to take a huge leap forward in year three.\n\nWilliams has had a shaky start to his NFL career. He started his career on IR due to a torn ACL in his final collegiate game. Williams got his first full offseason program before the 2023 season, but missed the first four games with a gambling suspension. These roadblocks kept Williams off the field and slowed his development as a pro.\n\nNone of these concern are holding Williams back anymore, which sets him up to have his first full year in the NFL in 2024.\n\nEarlier this offseason, Campbell was clear that he thinks Williams is ready for the challenge. In May, Campbell was asked to name the most improved Lions player during spring workouts. He named Jameson Williams right away.\n\n\"He's a man on a mission, and I'm just gonna leave it at that,\" Campbell said, per Colton Pouncey of The Athletic.\n\nWhen asked where exactly Williams has improved, Campbell replied: \"Everywhere.\"\n\nThis is a huge endorsement from Dan Campbell. It suggests that Williams is well on his way to becoming the player Detroit dreamed of getting in the draft a few years ago.\n\nWhat are realistic expectations for Jameson Williams in 2024?\n\nWe should start by saying that Williams doesn't need to be a hero. He just needs to get better and become a full-time starter with a clear role in the offense.\n\nWilliams does not need to make up for all of Reynolds' vacated production on his own. Second-year RB Jahmyr Gibbs was hailed as a \"position-less weapon\" by GM Brad Holmes after the 2023 NFL Draft and could become more involved in the passing attack. Sam LaPorta and Amon-Ra St. Brown could absorb some volume as well. There are also other role players like Kalif Raymond and Donovan Peoples-Jones who figure to do their fair share. Let's also not forget about David Montgomery and rookie running back/safety Sione Vaki.\n\nHowever, none of those players has the potential to open up Detroit's offense like Williams.\n\nIf Jameson Williams can become the dangerous deep threat that he was billed as coming out of college, he would add an entirely new element to the Lions' offense.\n\nA realistic expectation for Jamo in year three probably looks something like 50 catches for 800 yards and a handful of touchdowns. (AP) - Detroit Lions coach Dan Campbell stepped on a riser and stood behind a new, large lectern at the team's training facility.\n\n\"This is a huge podium,\" Campbell said Monday before the team's first training camp practice.\n\nExpectations are big for the Lions, too.\n\nDetroit is coming off its best season in generations, earning two playoff victories in one postseason for the first time since winning the 1957 NFL title.\n\nThe Lions are one of four franchises that haven't reached the Super Bowl, but they're No. 4 among favorites to reach the championship game, according to BetMGM Sportsbook.\n\nIt's easy to see what oddsmakers like about Detroit.\n\nDetroit Lions head coach Dan Campbell watches during an NFL football practice in Allen Park, Mich., Wednesday, July 24, 2024. (AP Photo/Paul Sancya)\n\nThe Lions have won 20 of their last 27 games in the regular season and are coming off a closely contested loss in the NFC championship game at San Francisco after leading the 49ers by 17 points in the third quarter.\n\nGeneral manager Brad Holmes made many moves to improve the team's chances of taking another step, strengthening weaknesses on both sides of the ball in free agency, a trade and the draft. Holmes also cut down potential distractions by giving quarterback Jared Goff, receiver Amon-Ra St. Brown and offensive tackle Penei Sewell new contracts.\n\n\"We know we can win a Super Bowl,\" St. Brown said. \"We have the team. We have the coaches. We have everything we need in this building to win a Super Bowl. That\u00b4s our goal. That\u00b4s our focus.\n\n\"Everything we do from here out moving forward is to get that Super Bowl.\"\n\nIf a Lions player said that a couple years ago, the response would've likely been laughter.\n\nCampbell's first team lost 13 games in 2021 - a fourth straight season with double-digit losses - and had setbacks in six of the first seven games the following year.\n\nSoon after Lions owner Sheila Ford Hamp refused to panic during the rough start in 2022, insisting she was confident in Holmes and Campbell, a franchise that has struggled to get it right for decades found a groove.\n\nDetroit closed that season with eight wins in 10 games, narrowly missing the playoffs, and picked up where it left off last year by matching a team record with 12 wins.\n\nThe Lions won a division title for the first time since 1993, beat the Matthew Stafford-led Los Angeles Rams for their first playoff victory in three-plus decades and eliminated Tampa Bay before falling one game short of the Super Bowl.\n\n\"We\u00b4re fortunate to have the success, but we know what came before that,\" said offensive tackle Taylor Decker, who endured a lot of losing after being drafted by Detroit in 2016. \" It was the work that came before that when no one cared what the Lions were doing.\"\n\nWhen the Lions kicked off training camp last year, Campbell asked the players to stand up, turn around and look toward the back of the full-team meeting room. They saw the team hadn't won a playoff game since 1992, a division title since 1993 and a league championship since 1957.\n\nAfter finally winning the division and a playoff game, offensive guard Graham Glasgow said the display was updated by someone who wrote 2023 on pieces of white, athletic tape.\n\n\"Those are still up there and there\u00b4s still tape through it with old-school tape,\" Campbell said. \"It just looks better that way.\n\n\"But we\u00b4ve checked the box on two and we\u00b4ve got one more to check.\"\n\nFollow Larry Lage at https://twitter/larrylage\n\nAP NFL: https://apnews.com/hub/nfl\n\nDetroit Lions quarterback Jared Goff (16) hands off to running back Jahmyr Gibbs (26) during an NFL football practice in Allen Park, Mich., Wednesday, July 24, 2024. Years of futility and disappointment made finding an optimistic, bullish take on the Lions ahead of training camp a rarity.\n\nNot anymore, certainly not after Detroit's 2023 campaign -- the best season for the Lions in the Super Bowl era. This summer, it's notable when an analyst pours some cold water on the fiery dreams and visions of Detroit grandeur for 2024. Yet we did manage to find one...\n\nNate Davis of USA TODAY is one of the few national analysts who has broken ranks with the Lions as the predicted winners of the NFC North. Davis instead projects the Green Bay Packers to take back the divisional crown in 2024, with the Lions finishing second. [affiliatewidget_smgtolocal]\n\nDavis does have the Lions finishing comfortably in the playoffs with a record of 11-6, good enough for the top wild card seed.\n\nThe rest of a division the Lions just won for the first time is also fast improving. A pathway to the first Super Bowl berth in franchise history likely requires a strong start as the Lions play just two home games over an eight-week period spanning October and November. But it could happen if a young core continues to blossom - WR Jameson Williams needs to step up - and reaps results from an upgraded pass defense.\n\nIn propping up the Packers, Davis notes their youth and also a change in defensive coordinator that Green Bay hopes overcome recent underachievement from that unit.\n\nExpanding out the projections, Davis has the Lions knocking off the NFC South champs, the Atlanta Falcons, in the wild card round game before succumbing to the Packers in Green Bay in the NFC Divisional Round.\n\nA quick check of last year's predictions shows Davis is not a Lions hater; he correctly pegged them as the NFC North champs, going 11-6. {"uri": "8241881124", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "20:03:09", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T20:03:09Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T20:02:20Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6431372761726379, "url": "https://www.nytimes.com/athletic/5655962/2024/07/24/detroit-lions-training-camp-dan-campbell-super-bowl/", "title": "Lions training camp notes: Dan Campbell vows team won't lose its identity, and more", "body": "ALLEN PARK, Mich. -- At the turn of the millennium, his second year in a league he's now been a part of for more than half of his life, a youthful Dan Campbell found himself on a roster ready to win. And win they did.\n\nThose Giants, coached by Jim Fassel, went 12-4 in 2000 -- winning the NFC East and the conference title, but ultimately falling short to the Baltimore Ravens in the Super Bowl. Naturally, there was hope for a return to the big stage the following season. The core remained in place. They believed they could run it back, and this time, win. But Campbell noticed a shift in energy ahead of it.\n\nA day in shorts instead of full pads was applauded by players. A practice ending early, celebrated. Campbell saw the little things adding up. He saw his team slowly lose its identity, ahead of a 7-9 season in 2001.\n\nThese days? He sees it as one of the best things that ever happened to him.\n\n\"I was a part of a team that, man, we did something really special,\" Campbell said. \"We came up a little short and the next year, we had the exact same team. The exact same team. ...And pretty soon, by the end of it, you just lost your identity and everything that made you what you are. You went away from it because, 'You know what? We'll be OK. We've got the same guys.' And that was a lesson learned for me. Because we were average. We went 7-9 the next year after going 12-4, and I will never forget that. Ever.\n\n\"So, we're not going to lose our identity. That is the most important thing to me, and I won't sacrifice it for anyone or anything.\"\n\nThat was Campbell's message to the Lions team he now coaches, having experienced the falloff firsthand as a player. It was in his head in Santa Clara, shortly after the Lions' 34-31 loss to the 49ers in the NFC Championship -- openly pondering if this was the last time he and his team would be here. Not because he doesn't think the Lions have what it takes to win. But because many have tried and failed to win it all after getting a taste. Some of those teams succumb to their own hype.\n\nAhead of his fourth training camp as a head coach, Campbell is trying to ensure these Lions don't. His players are with him.\n\n\"At this point, nobody cares what we did last year. It doesn't matter,\" Lions left tackle Taylor Decker said. \"It's gonna have no bearing on the season moving forward. If anything, it's going to make it harder for us. So, we can't take that for granted. It's hard to have a great season and then refocus and get back doing things the right way. But again, I think that goes back to Dan and Brad bringing in the right people who are culture fits, who won't let that happen. You have the right core group of guys, you're not going to let that happen. And I think we've got that.\"\n\nThe last thing Campbell wants is a complacent team. But by the looks of it, he doesn't have that.\n\nHe has a hungry one.\n\nThat's what we learned from the first day of training camp. Here's more.\n\nWords matter, and the Lions were very careful about the ones they used last year when describing their goals for the season. Back then, you didn't hear much external talk of a Super Bowl. And why would you? That 2022 team didn't even make the playoffs. The franchise hadn't won a division title in 30 years or a playoff game in 32.\n\nThere's a process to this, one they fully understood then. They had to crawl before they walked. But these days, they're up and running, and running things.\n\n\"You know, last year around this time, the year before, we were 9-8, barely missed the playoffs,\" Amon-Ra St. Brown said. \"So for us, I feel like going into last year it was like, 'Let's that's win the division, let's get into the playoffs and once we get there we can go get that Super Bowl. But our biggest goal (this year), our main goal, is the Super Bowl. I feel like everyone in the room is thinking the same way.\"\n\nThere is a difference. There's also a balancing act when speaking on those differences. This team proved it can compete last year. That's a box checked that's only going to give them something to fall back on in times of doubt. That's why experience is valuable, and the Lions gained that last season. Of course, you don't want to assume you'll be right back without putting in the work. However, the reason this team believes it can get back is because of just that -- how they prepare and how they're wired, along with some savvy moves made this offseason to get them that much closer.\n\nThat the Lions can now openly discuss their super-sized aspirations is the best sign of growth imaginable. Campbell mentioned the experience he, his staff and his team gained in January, and how it'll make everyone better. Decker said this team found its identity and now it's about consistency -- the mark of a good organization, in his mind. It's only been one day, but even this spring, the Lions carried themselves like a group that's been together and knows how to prepare.\n\nThe goal for any head coach is to assemble a self-policing locker room -- one that's so established and so strong culturally that new players can't help but fall in line and adapt to their surroundings. When you look around this Lions team -- from St. Brown to Penei Sewell to Jared Goff, Alex Anzalone, Aidan Hutchinson and more -- you can't help but see that. A business-like approach from this bunch. Even on a lighter Day 1, that was evident.\n\n\"We don't live off reputation, we live off of work,\" Campbell said. \"And that's what's gotten us where we're at. It's been a long, hard road to get to where we're at right now, and there's a price to be paid, and so we've got to go pay it again.\"\n\nOne of the Lions' biggest weaknesses last year was failing to generate much pressure outside of Hutchinson. Per Brett Kollman, Hutchinson generated 37.4 percent of the Lions' pressures last season. Typical elite edge rushers hover between the 27-30 percent range.\n\nIn other words, Hutchinson needs help. James Houston could be one to provide it.\n\nIn his first taste of action as a rookie in 2022, Houston recorded eight sacks in just seven games with a pass-rush win rate of 19.3 percent, per PFF -- good for 9th among all edge rushers. His 2023 season was cut short, but his win rate in two games (small sample size alert) was 23.1 percent. That's elite. If the Lions can get 200 pass-rush snaps out of Houston and he flirts with a win rate of 18-20 percent, he'll be able to help this group.\n\nSo I caught up with Houston one-on-one to see how he's feeling after an offseason to heal.\n\n\"I feel much better, man,\" Houston told me. \"I feel better than I did last year. I'm ready to go in the preseason with a little chip on my shoulder.\"\n\nThis offseason, Houston went to a few pass-rush summits -- one led by pass-rush specialist Brandon T. Jordan and another led by Von Miller. He said he was able to pick the brains of vets and learn how they approach the game. He called it \"instrumental\" for him to have that experience and hopes to put the tips he learned into practice this year.\n\nHouston said it was difficult watching the Lions' run without him -- perhaps even bittersweet. The team was successful in his absence, but it dearly missed his ability to get after the quarterback. And even when he returned for the NFC Championship game, he wasn't particularly close to 100 percent. That's why he's excited for what's ahead.\n\nThe current plan, Houston says, is to continue learning the Sam linebacker spot in Glenn's defense, while subbing in as a situational pass rusher. Don't expect him to be an every-down player, but he has the speed to make splash plays in this defense, and the finishing ability this roster sorely lacked last year.\n\nHe knows his job.\n\n\"They're looking for guys that are gonna be able to change the game -- get turnovers, ball production, so that's gonna have to be what I'll have to do,\" Houston said. \"Get to that quarterback, get the ball out.\"\n\n* The Lions will practice in shorts for the first four days of training camp. They'll be off on Sunday, before the first day of full pads on Monday.\n\n* Lions DT DJ Reader is healed from his torn quad, per Campbell. The next step is getting him up to speed and involved in competition, but the Lions won't rush him back to action. He's on track, though.\n\n* DB Brian Branch and Edge Marcus Davenport were both activated from the PUP list Wednesday, and participated in walkthroughs. Campbell said they're \"going slowly,\" as they're worked back into this mix. He thinks Davenport is closer than Branch to full strength, but they both participated a little bit in the meantime and are well on their way.\n\n* Speaking of Branch, I think we're starting to get some questions answered about his positional home this year. The Lions kicked things off with that walkthrough period, and Branch was next to Kerby Joseph at safety. So, this is looking like a thing. What might that mean for the rest of the secondary? Glad you asked.\n\n* Ifeatu Melifonwu would move to a reserve role -- and boy, is that some great depth. I'd still expect him to play semi-regular snaps depending on the look the offense presents. That's the value of Branch's flexibility, and his ability to move back to nickel on any play.\n\n* Today we saw Emmanuel Moseley at nickel, with Ennis Rakestraw Jr. and Terrion Arnold at outside corner. Part of that has to do with the absence of Carlton Davis III and Amik Robertson, who were placed on the active/NFI list and did not practice Wednesday, so the Lions were down some depth. If Branch to safety is a permanent thing, I think you'll see Davis and Arnold on the outside at corner, Robertson at nickel and Branch and Joseph at safety. Might be a way to get their best five on the field.\n\n* A couple more looks: When the Lions weren't playing with a nickel, they rotated a couple of Sam linebackers into the mix -- mainly Derrick Barnes and Houston. Levi Onwuzurike was playing some edge, a position he said the coaches wanted to see with him play this spring. With Reader out, Brodric Martin got a lot of interior reps at nose tackle. Too early to say if he's ready, but if he can be a rotational piece this year, that would be a boost.\n\n* Hutchinson had himself a day. During a three-play sequence, I credited him with a sack (or at the very least, a QB hit), a tackle for a short gain on a run play and another sack. This was against the first-team offense. He was going up against Penei Sewell, folks. Think he's in for a big year.\n\n* Jameson Williams cooked the defense during the first team period. Cooked. Initially lined up against Rakestraw (playing zone), Williams zoomed past Rakestraw, who passed him off to the safety Ifeatu Melifonwu on what looked like a deep post. Didn't stand a chance. Goff launched it, Williams tracked and caught it, then held out both arms in celebration and threw the ball at the fence in front of him. Here's the play:\n\n* Shortly thereafter, however, Williams puked. Something he ate, apparently. Very strange sequence. Still, a nice day for him. Here's St. Brown on Williams: \"He just looks more comfortable. He looks like he's done this before.\"\n\n* Josh Paschal quietly flashed a few times. I had him with a TFL and a sack during team periods. The Lions brought in competition for him with Davenport, so it's good to see him respond early.\n\n* I'll say this: both backup QBs looked good on Day 1. Hendon Hooker threw with zip and accuracy during his reps. He hit Daurice Fountain near the sideline for one of his more impressive throws. Ripped a crosser to Tom Kennedy over the middle for another nice gain. I liked what I saw. Nate Sudfeld also looked good. He threw a nice deep ball to Jalon Calhoun was solid for much of the day.
