Thanks to a young nucleus and plenty of veteran contributors, the Lions have a core in place that is capable of being among the league's elite.\n\nHowever, there are still uncertainties surrounding the roster. While several starters are viewed among the best at their respective positions, the depth on the roster remains a question in multiple areas.\n\nFor starters, there are unproven options set to potentially play key roles at wide receiver and defensive end. After Josh Reynolds left the Lions for the Broncos, Detroit's offense lost a very solid secondary pass-catching option.\n\nThere's plenty of expectations surrounding the potential development of Jameson Williams, and all signs point to him being the WR2. However, there is an ongoing battle for the third wide receiver position headlined by Kalif Raymond, Donovan Peoples-Jones and Antoine Green.\n\nPeoples-Jones and Green both had small roles last year, albeit for different reasons. Green was a rookie at the bottom of the depth chart, while Peoples-Jones took time to acclimate to the scheme after being acquired at the trade deadline.\n\nAt the receiver position, Amon-Ra St. Brown is the bona fide top option. However, the Lions are placing a lot in the hands of Williams developing into the second option. If he has hiccups throughout the year, the Lions' receiver depth will be tested.\n\nThe defensive end position is another that has questions. Like the receiver spot, the Lions have a top edge rusher in Aidan Hutchinson. Behind him, though, there are uncertainties.\n\nMarcus Davenport, the team's top free agent addition at the spot, will begin training camp on the Physically Unable to Perform list. While he can be activated at any time, there will be open opportunities in the meantime.\n\nJames Houston is a candidate to make an impact. Though he missed most of last season with an injury, the potential he showed in 2022 as a rookie was tantalizing.\n\nJosh Paschal could be another option, though he has made bigger impacts as a run defender throughout his first two NFL seasons. John Cominsky has a case, as does CFL standout Mathieu Betts.\n\nAnother avenue the Lions could explore is utilizing their interior defenders on the edge. Campbell hinted that the team had done so in the spring, as Levi Onwuzurike and rookie Mekhi Wingo both were options playing on the edge.\n\nIf Detroit does not feel as though their end options are satisfactory, using these bigger defenders on the edge could give the defense a unique look.\n\nOther positions with depth concerns include safety and tight end. Ifeatu Melifonwu and Kerby Joseph figure to be the team's starters, with Brian Branch also potentially entering the mix if the Lions elect to slide him from the nickel position.\n\nHowever, the top two options behind that trio are C.J. Moore and Brandon Joseph. Moore missed all of last year while serving a suspension, while Joseph is a 2023 UDFA who played two games as a practice squad elevation last year.\n\nThe tight end position is set to have a battle for the third spot behind Sam LaPorta and Brock Wright. James Mitchell holds weight as a 2022 fifth-round pick, but injuries have limited his impact.\n\nThe Lions brought back Shane Zylstra to compete for the job, as well as adding a pair of veterans in Parker Hesse and Sean McKeon. The dichotomy of the tight end room will create an interesting competition.\n\nUltimately, the Lions do have holes on their roster from a depth perspective. However, the holes are largely a result of inexperience or unproven players. That's what I'm looking for.\"\n\nBeyond Glenn, one of Campbell's first hires when he took over as Lions coach in 2021, and Johnson, who helped with play-calling duties after an in-season promotion that first year, the Lions return special teams coordinator Dave Fipp and top assistants Hank Fraley (offensive line), Kelvin Sheppard (linebackers), Antwaan Randle El (receivers) and Mark Brunell (quarterbacks) for their fourth seasons.\n\nMORE FROM BIRKETT: Detroit Lions training camp preview: Aiming for goal no NFL team has hit in 3 decades\n\nThey will have new faces in key places throughout the defense - free-agent additions D.J. Reader and Marcus Davenport are expected to play big roles up front for new defensive line coach Terrell Williams, and Carlton Davis III, Amik Robertson and rookie Terrion Arnold could start at cornerback under new secondary coach Deshea Townsend this fall - but the offensive nucleus remains largely intact and the Lions were able to keep another key offensive assistant this offseason despite job interest elsewhere.\n\nPassing game coordinator Tanner Engstrand was a candidate for offensive coordinator jobs with the New England Patriots, Tampa Bay Buccaneers and Seattle Seahawks this offseason.\n\nEngstrand said this spring he \"couldn't be happier to\" have remained in Detroit, though going through the interview process made him realize how far he's come as a coach.\n\n\"It's a little different place that being on the University of San Diego (staff) a few years back,\" Engstrand said in June. \"It's, we've come a long way in a short amount of time and we just, we look forward to what we have continuing to build and grow here and the opportunities that we're going to have here with this team.\"\n\nLike Campbell, Engstrand said he expects the Lions' unusual continuity to pay big dividends this fall.\n\n\"I think it's been fantastic because, again as coaches you're always coaching but last year there was a lot of coaching the coaches because they were new,\" he said. \"This year, everybody's on the same page, we all know what we're doing. We're able to jump into Year 3 in the offense and not necessarily be dragged, but bring it along slowly as we're teaching the players and the coaches. Now, the coaches are coaching the players as we go and everybody's really on the same page in continuity, understanding why we're doing things, what are the details, where do we need to be. And so I think that's been a huge advantage for us this spring, for sure.\"\n\nNo substitute for Sudfeld\n\nNate Sudfeld was not one of four players the Lions placed on a restricted list over the weekend, which should clear the way for him to compete with Hendon Hooker for the backup quarterback job at the start of camp.\n\nSudfeld tore his ACL in the Lions' preseason finale last year and missed all of the 2023 season. He spent most of the fall rehabbing in California, but returned to be around the team in the playoffs.\n\n\"There's no substitute for a veteran presence in that room, the experience that he has,\" Brunell said last month. \"Now, he hasn't played a lot but he's been around a lot. This is what Nate brings to the table: He's been in multiple systems, he is a hard-working guy with a great attitude. He's excellent in the room, he's excellent in the locker room, guys like him. But he's very smart. He understands situational football as well as anybody I've been around.\"\n\nHooker is expected to take the bulk of the second-team and preseason reps as the Lions groom the 2023 third-round pick for a roster spot. But for one of the NFC's leading Super Bowl contenders, Sudfeld might offer the Lions better insurance.\n\nAn eight-year NFL veteran who saw limited playing time with the Lions as a backup in 2022, Sudfeld was a limited participant in OTAs and June minicamp.\n\nTHIS IS WHY YOU HAVE DEPTH: Lions place D.J. Reader, Marcus Davenport, Brian Branch on PUP list to start training camp\n\n\"We ask a lot of our quarterbacks at the line of scrimmage and in the huddle,\" Brunell said. \"We ask our guys to get us into the right play, and so if you have a play and there's a problem over there, you got to be able to fix it. And within the parameters of the play, we have the opportunity to go from one play to the next depending on what we're seeing. Ninety-nine percent of the time, Nate is right.\n\n\"He understands defenses. He knows what to look for. He's just very, very smart, and he can get you into the right play and that's half the battle. If you can do that, and then you go execute it, you're going to move the team. And so having him in the room with that ability and his ability to work well with the other guys and be a resource for Jared, much like David Blough was last year and much like Nate has been, having those guys in the room is a huge asset for the quarterback and the quarterback coach, really.\"", "source": {"uri": "freep.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Detroit Free Press"}, "authors": [], "concepts": [{"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aaron_Glenn", "type": "person", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Aaron Glenn"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dan_Campbell", "type": "person", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Dan Campbell"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detroit_Lions", "type": "wiki", "score": 5, "label": {"eng": "Detroit Lions"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lineman_(gridiron_football)", "type": "wiki", "score": 3, "label": {"eng": "Lineman (gridiron football)"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Fipp", "type": "person", "score": 3, "label": {"eng": "Dave Fipp"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hank_Fraley", "type": "person", "score": 3, "label": {"eng": "Hank Fraley"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Brunell", "type": "person", "score": 3, "label": {"eng": "Mark Brunell"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Football_Conference", "type": "wiki", "score": 3, "label": {"eng": "National Football Conference"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Defensive_coordinator", "type": "wiki", "score": 3, "label": {"eng": "Defensive coordinator"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_football_positions", "type": "wiki", "score": 3, "label": {"eng": "American football positions"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amik_Robertson", "type": "person", "score": 2, "label": {"eng": "Amik Robertson"}}, {"uri": "http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D._J._Reader", "type": "person", "score": 2, "label": {"eng": "D. It's been a long, hard road to get to where we're at right now, and there's a price to be paid and so we've got to go pay it again. That's the message, and it will always be the message.\"\n\nAs the Lions enter the 2024 season with the third-best chance to reach the Super Bowl at 17.6%, according to ESPN Analytics, Campbell continues to drive that gritty mindset that helped Detroit reach this point.\n\nOnce veterans reported to training camp Tuesday night at the newly named Meijer Performance Center, Campbell's message was to stay committed to putting the work into position themselves for a championship.\n\n\"I believe that what we did last year can carry over into this season. I do, as long as we go to work,\" Campbell said.\n\nThe Lions also are favored to win their division for the second consecutive season, which has only happened once in franchise history when they captured titles from 1952-54. However, the Lions have never won 10 or more games in back-to-back seasons; they are one of only two active franchises, along with the Carolina Panthers, to never accomplish this feat.\n\nEntering Year 4, Campbell feels he's a better coach than last year because he's \"more experienced.\" With increased expectations, the Lions coaching staff is also committed to improving after a making noise around the league with risky play-calling under Campbell, notably on fourth downs.\n\nThe Lions \"went for it\" on 34% of their fourth downs last season, the highest percentage in a season by any team since at least 2000.\n\n\"I've got more experience, but so does the staff under me,\" Campbell said. \"They've got more experience, and they've got more experience being around me and myself being around them, so that makes me better. Your staff makes you a lot better, and they're the reason that I'm even in this position and we're having success. {"uri": "2024-07-430797524", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "11:19:09", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T11:19:09Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T11:19:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6078431606292725, "url": "https://www.industriesnews.net/news/274465983/5-things-to-watch-2024-training-camp", "title": "5 things to watch: 2024 training camp", "body": "The rookies, quarterbacks and players rehabbing injuries have been in Allen Park for a few days now, but training camp really gets underway when the veterans report Tuesday and practice kicks off Wednesday.\n\nDetroit enters 2024 as one of the favorites to represent the NFC in the Super Bowl in February, but first the foundation must be laid and that begins with training camp over the next month.\n\nHere are five things I'll be looking out for when camp kicks off this week:\n\n1. Cornerback competition\n\nThe Lions completely revamped the cornerback room, acquiring Carlton Davis via trade, signing Amik Robertson in free agency, and bringing back Emmanuel Moseley, all before drafting Terrion Arnold in the first round and Ennis Rakestraw Jr. in the second round of this year's NFL Draft.\n\nJust how will roles and playing time shake out? Davis enters camp at one of the outside spots. Arnold was opposite him with the first-team defense during OTAs and minicamp and we could certainly see that combo on the outside to start camp.\n\nBrian Branch is currently on Active/PUP, but when he returns the Lions play to use his versatility a little more than they did his rookie season by adding some safety to his duties. He will still see time at nickel, where he thrived as a rookie. How will reps for Robertson and Rakestraw shake out? Both have the versatility to play inside and outside. Will Moseley be ready to go at the start of camp coming off his second straight ACL tear, and what will he look like when he does get on the field? Don't forget he was a starter on the outside for a very good 49ers defense in 2022.\n\nNo position group went through more change than the cornerback room this offseason. Detroit looks to be much more talented with better depth, and the competition for playing roles and roster spots is expected to be fierce. Coaches are hoping that makes everyone better.\n\n2. Second-year players\n\nRunning back Jahmyr Gibbs, tight end Sam LaPorta and linebacker Jack Campbell made the Pro Football Writers Association All-Rookie Teams, while Branch was arguably one of the best nickel cornerbacks in the league last season.\n\nGibbs, LaPorta and Branch combined for 22 touchdowns, the most from a Lions rookie class since 1934. Gibbs and LaPorta were the NFL's first set of rookie teammates to each produce 10 touchdowns in their first season. Campbell recorded the second most tackles by a rookie (89) and was the only rookie to record at least 80 tackles, five tackles for loss and have 2.0 sacks on the season.\n\nWe typically see players take their biggest leap in development in their second season as the game slows down for them after a entire year in the league under their belt. If that's true for this second-year crew, what kind of numbers could they produce?\n\nI'll definitely have a little closer eye on Campbell, who is expected to take over the MIKE job on a full-time basis.\n\n\"Let me tell you first off he's a man,\" Lions defensive coordinator Aaron Glenn said of Campbell this offseason. \"He's a grown man. He's really taken control of this offseason the way he should take control of it.\n\n\"He's a true MIKE backer. He's a guy that lives, breathes green dot mentality as a MIKE linebacker. He's done a really good job - all our guys have - of transforming their body because they've had a true offseason in the NFL.\"\n\nAnother second-year player to watch is quarterback Hendon Hooker, who is competing with veteran Nate Sudfeld to be Jared Goff's backup.\n\n2024 training camp preview: Special teams 2024 training camp preview: Offensive line Lions place 3 players on PUP & 1 on NFI ahead of training camp\n\n3. Kicker competition\n\nCan the incumbent Michael Badgley, a reliable player down the stretch for Detroit last season and during their playoff run, hold off big-legged UFL sensation Jake Bates, who stood out with the Michigan Panthers this spring.\n\nBadgley is a career 82.4 percent field goal kicker but has just five makes on 13 attempts from 50-plus yards. He did make a critical 54-yard field goal to help propel the Lions past the Los Angeles Rams in the playoffs last season. Bates made 77.3 percent of his attempts (17-for-22), but four of those misses came from 50-plus yards. He also had makes from 64, 62 and 60 yards.\n\nWill consistency and experience win out or can the youngster step in and win the job? Expect head coach Dan Campbell and special teams coordinator Dave FIpp to put both kickers in as many pressure situations as they can think up in camp. The preseason games will be huge for both players as well. The new kickoff rules and the accuracy of placing the football in the landing zone could also factor into the competition.\n\n4. Depth along both lines\n\nThe starters upfront along both the offensive and defensive lines is pretty well set, but what will the depth in the trenches look like?\n\nThe offensive line is arguably the top unit in the league led by tackle Penei Sewell and center Frank Ragnow, considered by most to be the best in the league at their respective positions. Last season, the Lions faced a number of injuries upfront but players like Graham Glasgow, Kayode Awosika and Dan Skipper stepped in and the unit didn't skip a beat. Can Christian Mahogany push Awosika, Sorsdal and others for a role? And when Giovanni Manu returns from Active/NFI, can he take big enough strides in camp to be a depth player?\n\nOn defense, Aidan Hutchinson, Alim McNeill, DJ Reader and Marcus Davenport make up a formidable front four. Reader isn't ready to start camp (Active/PUP) as he's still rehabbing a torn quad suffered last season. That could give young players like Brodric Martin, Chris Smith and Mekhi Wingo an opportunity to show what they can do inside early on. Can Levi Onwuzurike finally break through and be the player the Lions thought he could be when they selected him in the second round in 2021?\n\nDetroit needs more production opposite Hutchinson on the edge and are hoping the veteran Davenport can make a significant impact in that department when he returns from Active/PUP, but can others like John Cominsky, Josh Paschal and James Houston be part of that conversation too? When the pads come on after the acclimation period we'll start to get answers to what Detroit's depth upfront on both sides of the ball will look like.\n\n5. Jamo development\n\nDetroit's offense was one of the best in the NFL last season and more of the same is expected from that side of the ball. What could take Ben Johnson's offense to a new level is if third-year wide receiver Jameson Williams becomes the player the Lions drafted him to be in 2022 (12th overall).\n\nWilliams had a red-shirt year of sorts his first season recovering from a torn ACL suffered in college. He was suspended the first month of last season and dealt with some early injuries, but really came on strong at the end of the year. We can count on one hand the number of players in this league with the kind of speed Williams has, but can he be a complete weapon at the position in Year 3?\n\nHe's going to see a significant rise in snaps as the No. 2 option at receiver behind Amon-Ra St. Brown. Will we also see a significant uptick in targets and receptions? If he becomes a consistent weapon all over the field - not just on the go balls - Detroit's offense has the potential to be the most explosive unit in the league.", "source": {"uri": {"uri": "2024-07-430150541", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-22", "time": "20:23:23", "dateTime": "2024-07-22T20:23:23Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-22T20:12:10Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6039215922355652, "url": "https://eu.detroitnews.com/story/sports/nfl/lions/2024/07/22/lions-training-camp-preview-5-potential-x-factors-to-watch/74498083007/", "title": "Lions training camp preview: 5 potential X-factors to watch", "body": "It became more and more apparent throughout the Detroit Lions' 2023 training camp that Brian Branch was on a trajectory to have an excellent rookie season.\n\nThough the Lions' secondary struggled all season long, Branch was a bright spot. He was excellent in every phase, providing stability to a secondary that was always searching for more.\n\nWho will those players be this season? The ones who hold some intrigue, but could vault into sky-high expectations by the time Week 1 rolls around? Let's look at five potential X-factors to watch in Lions training camp.\n\n\u25b6 Jameson Williams, receiver\n\nSince the day he was drafted with the 12th pick in 2022, Williams has been a lightning rod. His combination of speed and athleticism is so unique that it's hard to remember a time when Lions fans were so excited about seeing a draft pick on the field. The first time he entered a game, the crowd literally chanted his name.\n\nBut Williams' trajectory as a pro has not been linear. He's had outbursts of production and has provided peeks at his incredibly high ceiling, but sports are about consistency, and he struggled to find that through his first couple of years, as injuries and a gambling suspension halted his year-two development at a critical time.\n\nThe Lions' reluctance to add another top receiver into the mix -- especially in the wake of a departing Josh Reynolds -- indicates that they believe Williams is ready to be a top guy in 2024, and through the offseason program, he showed why. His chemistry with quarterback Jared Goff is clearly better than ever and he's shown vast improvement tracking the ball downfield. Though this list is in no particular order, we'd put Williams in the top spot if we had to rank them.\n\n\u25b6 Jack Campbell, linebacker\n\nIt wasn't easy for Campbell to see the field after being a first-round pick a year ago, but that wasn't necessarily a knock on his game. Off-ball linebacker is arguably the most difficult position to adjust to when going from college to the pros, and the Lions were getting quality play from Alex Anzalone and Derrick Barnes.\n\nBut linebackers coach Kelvin Sheppard was adamant that Campbell is a man possessed entering Year 2, showing massive improvements as a leader of the defense through the offseason program. Like Williams, it's obvious what Campbell's size and athleticism can provide to his unit. And with the mental side coming along, it's hard not to be intrigued by what he's able to show in camp.\n\n\u25b6 Ifeatu Melifonwu, safety\n\nThere's been plenty of excitement behind the idea of what Brian Branch can be in his second year, but one defensive back whose potential doesn't get nearly enough shine is Melifonwu. After finally getting healthy for the final stretch of the year, there were few players in football who were more impactful. He had three sacks, 26 tackles, two interceptions, seven pass deflections and a forced fumble in his last five games alone.\n\nNot only that, but his versatility will allow the Lions to get creative with disguises and keep Melifonwu on the field, using him and Branch as a pair of Swiss Army Knives to keep offenses guessing. 52.5% of his defensive snaps last season came in the box and slot corner. Following a successful playoff run and healthy offseason, it's possible he's one of the stars of training camp. Branch would be a good candidate for this list, too, but he's going to begin camp on the injury list (and you likely already know that he's oozing with potential in year two).\n\n\u25b6 Josh Paschal, defensive lineman\n\nPaschal's injury history caused him to get a slow start on his Lions career, but toward the end of last season -- and before he got hurt at the beginning of the year -- Paschal showed flashes of why the Lions drafted him with a second-round pick in 2022.\n\nAfter his first two seasons, there's some belief that Paschal has a better chance of making contributions inside, but he was drafted as an edge defender and that is, in fact, where he played a majority of his defensive snaps last season.\n\nWith EDGE Marcus Davenport and defensive tackle DJ Reader both starting camp on the injury list, Paschal will have plenty of opportunity to show what he can do all along the offensive line. It also doesn't hurt that the Lions this offseason hired what many believe to be one of the best defensive line coaches in the NFL, Terrell Williams.\n\n\u25b6 Sione Vaki, running back\n\nThis one is kind of off the wall, and even if we're just looking at the rookie class, there's probably a player or two on defense who could ultimately have more of an immediate, team-wide impact. But there's just something about the ceiling of Vaki; he's an explosive play waiting to happen. He can do it as a running back. He can do it as a receiver. He can do it on kick returns.\n\nBut above all, the most exciting thing about Vaki is that he'll spend his first year in the NFL under the tutelage of offensive coordinator Ben Johnson. Last year, the Lions slow-played the involvement of rookie running back Jahmyr Gibbs, so maybe we won't see Vaki really come on until the second half of the season. But they also realized they could throw Sam LaPorta straight into the fire and did so without hesitation. If Vaki can gain the trust of the coaching staff and quarterback Jared Goff, it seems like there's no limit to what the Lions can do with him.", "source": {"uri": "detroitnews.com", "dataType": Coming off a trip to the NFC Championship Game last season, there are among the top Super Bowl favorites heading into the 2024 season. Four categories were used, and weighted to create an overall score: Roster (minus the quarterback), the quarterback, coaching and front office.\n\nThe Lions come in at No. 4, behind the Kansas City Chiefs, Baltimore Ravens and Buffalo Bills, with a an overall score of 88.9. Their overall roster (minus quarterback), coaching and front office scores were all top-six, while their quarterback score was 12th.\n\nGraziano lauded the Lions' offense and the culture Dan Campbell has built. {"uri": "2024-07-430123485", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-22", "time": "19:41:43", "dateTime": "2024-07-22T19:41:43Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-22T19:36:53Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5803921818733215, "url": "https://clutchpoints.com/why-lions-aidan-hutchinson-doesnt-want-to-say-super-bowl", "title": "Why Lions' Aidan Hutchinson doesn't want to say 'Super Bowl'", "body": "What held the star defensive end back from making a bold prediction?\n\nLast season, the Detroit Lions got so close to the Super Bowl they could taste it. But they remained on the unwanted list of teams that have never made it. So can defensive end Aidan Hutchinson be blamed for treading lightly when discussing the Lions' hopes for the 2024 NFL season?\n\nAppearing on the Rich Eisen Show, Hutchinson didn't say two important words when asked what he visualized for the Lions' final game.\n\n\"I'm visualizing the Honolulu blue, the white little confetti coming down and doing some snow angels,\" Hutchinson said. \"That's the visualization.\"\n\nBut what does Lions DE Aidan Hutchinson really think?\n\nPressure comes in all forms in the NFL. Hutchinson apparently didn't want to add to the mix.\n\n\"There's a lot of expectations and pressure but I really do believe this team can get it done,\" he said. \"And I feel like myself, as an individual I've mentally prepared myself to be playing until February this year.\n\n\"All of my regimens and running, I'm getting ready to have my body going until February. It's a very realistic thing, and it's something that's not too far out there. It's something very much within grasp.\"\n\nThe experts -- including nfl.com -- seem to agree, slotting the Lions at No. 4 in the post-draft power rankings. Detroit got receiver Amon-Ra St. Brown and tackle Penei Sewell under comfortable contract extensions, and beefed up their secondary weakness with first-round pick CB Terrion Arnold. Then they added CB Ennis Rakestraw Jr. in round two. Also, Detroit added DT Mekhi Wingo and guard Christian Mahogany, drafting like a team with win-now aspirations.\n\nSo Detroit fans probably don't have any problem with Hutchinson cutting loose with a bold prediction. Eventually, Hutchinson gave in and told Eisen, \"I feel like a lot of guys are saying Super Bowl this, and Super Bowl that, but what gives me a lot of joy is I know when those seconds are ticking down, confetti's falling, you take that deep breath knowing you did it, that's what I look forward to.\"\n\nHutchinson has lived up to the billing of being the No. 2 overall pick in 2022. He finished second in the AP defensive rookie of the year voting with 9.5 sacks, 52 tackles, and a surprising three interceptions. Year two brought more good stuff, including his first Pro Bowl appearance. Hutchinson totaled 11.5 sacks and met his tackle quota with 51. He picked off another pass and forced three fumbles.\n\nStill, it's Detroit\n\nEven the great running back Barry Sanders couldn't get the Lions to the big game. Detroit remains one of four teams without a Super Bowl trophy. The others are the Browns, Texans and Jaguars. So even talking about the Super Bowl, with the 2024 roster looking nice and last year's experience to grow on, makes for fun times in Detroit.\n\nHead coach Dan Campbell famously said the Lions might have missed their best chance to reach the big game. But Hutchinson told Pro Football Talk Campbell's comments came out of the tough blow of the close loss to the 49ers in the NFC Championship -- a game the Lions led 24-7 at halftime. Hutchinson said the entire Lions team deal with raw emotions after the game.\n\n\"I don't know if he meant those things completely, because in our exit meetings the day after, he's like, 'We're going to the Super Bowl next year!' Hutchinson said. \"Like, 'I don't care what it takes!' You kind of hear that after the game, and you get a little discouraged because you're like, 'Do you think that was our only shot?' I think it was just an emotional thing. I get it because it's like you have this 22-week season, and you're so close and you just miss out.\n\n\"The next day, he kind of came in and gave us this speech that we're like, we're all ready to play again right now. I believe it too, because all the players that we have that are talented on our team are so young and we have so many more years all playing together.\"", "source": {"uri": "clutchpoints.com", After winning the first division title in three decades and making a run to the NFC Championship game last season, confidence is aplenty inside the walls of the team's Allen Park facility.\n\nAmong those feeling the new wave of confidence is wide receiver Amon-Ra St. Brown, who is coming off an All-Pro season. Having been with the team since the start of the Dan Campbell era, the USC product is part of the core foundation that has been essential to the recent success.\n\nAfter surprising some last year with postseason success, the Lions are not running from expectations. Rather, leaders such as St. Brown are embracing the hype and using it as fuel.\n\n\"I think we're really confident. Each year, you get into that meeting on the first day and it's like, 'What do you want to accomplish as a team?' I can truthfully say this year, it's not even playoffs,\" St. Brown said. \"It's not (being the) number one seed, it's the Super Bowl. That's the feeling with everyone in the room. Personally, I feel like truly as a team, we all feel the same way. We all want to win the Super Bowl, we know we can win the Super Bowl. We have the team, we have the coaches. We have everything we need in this building to win a Super Bowl. That's our goal, that's our focus, and everything we do from here on moving forward is to get that Super Bowl.\"\n\nLast season, the Lions entered training camp with a more moderate sense of hype. They finished the 2022 season on a winning surge, and the belief was that the team would prove its legitimacy as a contender by winning their division in 2023.\n\nThey did just that, then rode a wave of momentum through the first two rounds of the playoffs before an untimely collapse against the San Francisco 49ers. Now, the team knows what it is capable of and is setting high goals as a result.\n\n\"Last year around this time, the year before we were 9-8, barely missed the playoffs,\" St. Brown said. \"So for us, I feel like going into last year it was like, 'Let's win the division, let's get into the playoffs and once we get there, we can go get that Super Bowl.'\n\n\"Last year, let's win the division, get to the playoffs and hopefully once we get there we can go make a run at it. This year, it's like, obviously you can't win the Super Bowl without making the playoffs. Number one seed, all that stuff sounds good, but our main goal is the Super Bowl. I feel like everyone in the room is thinking the same way. I think just the thought alone is that it means a lot.\"\n\nOne more box to check\n\nLast season, the Lions made a point of acknowledging how long it had been since the franchise previously won both a division title and a playoff game. The years of each time they'd last accomplished those feats lined the back of the team meeting room.\n\nNow, after the Lions did both last season, those numbers have been taped over. However, the Lions know that in order to reach the ultimate goal, they will have to once again take the previous two steps.\n\n\"Those are still up there, and there's still taped through with old school tape. It just looks better that way. But we've checked the box on two, and we've got one more to check,\" Campbell said. \"But to get there, we've got to check those first two one more time and update them. Everything starts with finding a way to win your division. You do that, you've got to put in the work, man. You've got to find a way to win the first game of the season and then you go from there.\"\n\nThis focus points to the larger mindset echoed by St. Brown, who believes that the Lions have what it takes to set themselves apart from the rest of the league.\n\nEvery team enters the season with high expectations, but the Lions feel as though their blend of experience and talent give them a chance to make good on the hype surrounding them this offseason.\n\n\"I think we all know what the goal is. It doesn't need to be said. We all, in the room, as a team, we've got one goal, and that's the Super Bowl,\" St. Brown stated. \"We're not looking any further, we're not looking anywhere else. Obviously you've got to take it one game at a time every week, we understand that. The end goal, I think for every team, is to win the Super Bowl. But some teams it's just different. {"uri": "2024-07-432666734", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-25", "time": "00:21:06", "dateTime": "2024-07-25T00:21:06Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-25T00:09:07Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5568627715110779, "url": "https://eu.detroitnews.com/story/sports/columnists/bob-wojnowski/2024/07/24/wojo-dan-campbell-determined-to-keep-detroit-lions-lean-and-mean/74525921007/", "title": "Wojo: Dan Campbell determined to keep Lions lean and mean, not fat and sassy", "body": "Allen Park -- The Lions were 12-5 last season and many objective observers think they'll win 12 again, or maybe 13. Or perhaps 11. Or worst-case scenario, 10.\n\nOf course there's no guarantee they'll take the next step from the NFC Championship Game to the Super Bowl because climbs aren't always smooth and linear. But there's no way the Lions could drop, say, from 12 victories to seven, right?\n\nNah. Too talented, too deep, too motivated. That's the encouraging part, the one Dan Campbell is counting on. And then there's the scary part, the one Campbell has seen, and lived.\n\nWhen training camp opened Wednesday, Campbell delivered a few pointed messages, including one that came straight from the gut. He was a third-year tight end for the New York Giants in 2001 when they were coming off a 12-4 season and a Super Bowl appearance. The defense was menacing and Jim Fassel was an accomplished coach entering his fifth season.\n\nSuper Bowl aspirations melted to a 7-9 record, and the decline was gradual but visible. Campbell saw it then, and never forgot it. He said workouts ran a little shorter, to give veteran players more rest. Padded practices weren't as fierce. The edge started to fade, and the Giants plummeted as if in slow motion.\n\n\"It's one of the best things that ever happened to me,\" Campbell said Wednesday. \"We did something really special and came up a little short, and the next year we had the exact same team. ... And pretty soon, by the end of it, you've lost your identity and everything that made you what you are. You went away from it because, 'You know what? We'll be OK. We've got the same guys.'\"\n\nCampbell is big on messages, and this is one he's hammering to a team that's 22-8 since mid-2022 and has most of the same guys, and more. He's not trying to scare anyone. He's not downplaying the Lions' chances. He's explaining something most people don't understand unless they've been through it.\n\n\"That was a lesson learned for me (in 2001),\" Campbell said. \"We went 7-9 the year after going 12-4 and I will never forget that. Ever. So we're not going to lose our identity. That is the most important thing to me, and I won't sacrifice it for anyone or anything.\"\n\nBack to work\n\nIn his three seasons here, Campbell has delivered a consistent message -- \"We don't live off reputation, we live off of work,\" he reiterated. The Lions have become experienced with success, and are learning to handle it.\n\nEarly indications are, complacency won't be a problem. If it becomes one, Campbell has the voice to stamp it out, as do many of the players. This is a young group with the right mix of humility and hunger. Its leader, Jared Goff, has taken more hits (verbal and otherwise) than any $53-million-per-year quarterback should. He figures the Lions have more of their own to deliver.\n\n\"Yeah, we've got a target on our backs now,\" Goff said. \"But we certainly have our list of people we got a target on. Teams that maybe still don't respect us. Teams that have said certain things in the past. It's not like we're at the top of the mountain looking down. We're constantly feeling like we're the underdog and have to fight for what we deserve, fight for our respect.\"\n\nGoff wouldn't identify the Lions' primary targets, but you can guess a few. NFC North rivals for sure, especially the Packers, who are stirring with quarterback Jordan Love. Gotta be the Cowboys, too, who often beat the Lions in bizarre and controversial ways. Naturally the 49ers and maybe the Seahawks, a persistent nemesis.\n\nHumility and hunger can be a lethal combination. Campbell endured a 4-19-1 start here with players hardened by it. It's no accident those early survivors -- Goff, Penei Sewell, Aidan Hutchinson, Amon-Ra St. Brown -- are a huge part of what could be next, and they sound ready for it.\n\nWhat would make this season a success?\n\n\"I think the obvious answer would be a Super Bowl,\" Hutchinson said. \"That's the expectation, and if we fall short, if we end up in the same spot, it'd be a failure for sure. That is the mentality, and it's kind of a harsh mentality. But we have the guys and there's no reason we shouldn't be playing in that game and winning that game.\"\n\nHutchinson has believed in himself and his team since his Michigan days, when he helped beat Ohio State and changed the program's culture. He turns 24 next month, and still finds it hard to fathom how much he's gained entering his third NFL season.\n\nThe Lions bet big on Goff, Sewell and St. Brown with contract extensions. They're betting on Hutchinson too, and he'll take that wager. With Aaron Glenn ramping up the aggressive play-calling, and veterans DJ Reader and Marcus Davenport added to a defensive line that includes Alim McNeill, that group could make the biggest leap.\n\n\"I know I'm the guy that people are gonna rely on,\" Hutchinson said. \"I know I'm the guy that's gonna face the most expectations and pressure, and I've really learned to embrace that. The biggest difference in my mentality is, when it's the fourth quarter and someone's got to make a play, and everyone's looking at me, I say bring it on.\"\n\nCrush complacency\n\nWell, bring it on indeed. The franchise has prepped for increased attention, even adding double-decker stands around the practice field, newly christened the Meijer Performance Center.\n\nOn the first day of camp, it was overcast and mild, with hotter, tougher days ahead. The Lions have dutifully watched tape of the collapse against the 49ers in the conference title game, when a 24-7 halftime lead turned into a crushing 34-31 loss. Goff said it's hard but \"you think about it every day.\" Campbell said he only watches the second half because the first half was \"irrelevant.\"\n\nFeel the pain so you don't forget it. Build on the reputation so you don't lose it. Campbell didn't intend to impugn Fassel (who's deceased) with his example of a team letting up. He looks like he's done this before. He looks like he knows what to expect.\"\n\nLions quarterback Jared Goff and Williams also showed a strong connection.\n\nGoff hit Williams on some nice sideline routes in individual drills - Williams got in and out of his breaks fast, showed improved hands, stronger body control and nice footwork.\n\n\"I'm getting better every day,\" Williams said.\n\nFacing the defense, Goff hit Williams on beautiful post pattern for a touchdown - Williams simply split the defensive backs and blew the top off the defense.\n\n\"I'm just excited to be playing ball,\" Williams said. \"Trying to make plays - that's it.\"\n\nBACK. TO. WORK: Priority No. 1 for Detroit Lions at start of training camp? Avoid complacency\n\nEntering his third season, Williams is expected to play a more critical role this fall.\n\nHis first season was slowed because of a knee injury, and last season was stunted because of a gambling suspension.\n\nNow, he should be full go for the first time in his career.\n\n\"The biggest thing I'd probably say is confidence,\" David Montgomery said of Williams. \"He was doing special things in college, but to see him here in person from the first year that I was here to now, it's a big, big improvement. And, you know, his body's changed too.\"\n\nAfter catching a long touchdown pass, he lost his cookies, not to mention his breakfast.\n\nBut this didn't appear to be a player who had to vomit in the middle of practice for being out of shape, which is hardly unusual for the first day of training camp.\n\nNo.\n\nThis looked like somebody who was working so hard, playing with so much intensity, running all around the field - excited for the first practice and a significantly new and improved role - that it got the better of him.\n\n\"Ah, I just ate the wrong thing this morning,\" Williams said, walking into the facility.\n\nAnother lesson learned.\n\n\"He's not that young rookie guy anymore,\" St. Brown said. \"He's been here for a few years. Every year he just gets more comfortable. And I know I've been saying this every year but I think I'm he's gotten better every year, obviously. But I think this year is gonna be huge for him.\"\n\nHow does the Lions' defense look early on?\n\nThe first defenders on the field during the seven-on-seven portion of practice were Derrick Barnes at left linebacker, Jack Campbell at middle and Alex Anzalone at right linebacker. Ennis Rakestraw Jr. and Terrion Arnold were at corner with Kerby Joseph and Ifeatu Melifonwu at safety. Emmanuel Moseley replaced Barnes as the slot corner for a nickel set. Rakestraw also took reps at slot cornerback with the second-team defense.\n\nJoseph praised the new additions to the defensive backfield for eagerly looking to improve.\n\n\"I love their sense of urgency and their work ethic,\" Joseph said about the rookie corners. \"Everybody wants to get better. Everybody wants to work hard, no matter what round they went in or who they are. They keep their head down and they are humble.\"\n\nIT STILL GRINDS YOUR GEARS: 25 years after Barry Sanders' retirement, he -- and Detroit Lions -- still owe an apology\n\nTaylor Decker got more dry needlers. Well, the Lions' left tackle wasn't the only player who requested a few more folks who could perform the muscle-related restorative therapy. Nor were dry needlers Decker's only request.\n\nHe asked for a few more athletic trainers as well. And got those too. His requests came out of an organizational effort to update and renovate the training facilities at the team's headquarters in Allen Park.\n\nAnd for Decker, the effort sent a powerful message:\n\n\"We are going to give everything we can back to you.\"\n\nThe \"reinvestment,\" as he called it, is most notable in the team's new athletic training room, replete with the latest equipment, technology, and much more spacious.\n\nFor Decker, and surely for his teammates, finding more efficient ways to minimize injury and recover from injuries could offer a slight competitive advantage over the season.\n\nEven, he said, if that advantage amounts only to one or two percent.\n\n\"Got to stay healthy, got to get back on the field,\" he said.\n\nIn a game decided by the tiniest of margins, the Lions, and Decker, hope they just increased theirs.\n\nHendon Hooker's hot start\n\nQuarterback Hendon Hooker was beaming as he came off the field, rightly excited to talk about performing well in his first NFL training camp practice. We've been talking about the Lions' 2023 third-round for so long that it's easy to forget he missed all of camp last year while he covered from a torn ACL in November 2022.\n\nHe had a full offseason this year and looked sharp as the No. 2 on Wednesday, taking snaps ahead of Nate Sudfeld. Hooker tossed some nice, crisp sideline passes to Amon-Ra St. Brown, Jalon Calhoun and Kalif Raymond and was quick and steady in the pocket.\n\n\"I really haven't played to the best of my ability that I know I can play until now,\" he said. \"So going through this offseason I was just really amped up to get back out here and showcase my talent.\n\n\"So really that first team (period) I was too jittery and too amped up. So once I relaxed and I got into my groove you could really see the ball coming out on time and smoother drops. I was in control of the huddle and felt great after that first team (period).\"\n\nExpect Hooker and Sudfeld to alternate as the No. 2, which should make their camp battle fun. Both made some great throws, with one of Sudfeld's best coming on an over-the-shoulder pass to Zonovan Knight, who beat safety Loren Strickland for a big gain in a 4-minute drill.\n\n\"Competition makes the room better,\" Hooker said. \"So continue to push off Jared, continue to push off Nate, and then the coaching has been great. So I'm just learning and staying consistent every day.\"\n\nGrand new seating\n\nFans planning to attend an open practice will be pleasantly surprised when they see the upgraded covered seating they get to enjoy.\n\nThe bleachers have been replaced in the general-admission section with two large grandstands that accommodate 2,500 fans and feature stadium-style chair backs. There's also a two-story VIP tent that looks more like a small building and also has stadium seating.\n\nThe first open practice is Saturday for season-ticket holders and \"Lions Loyal Members.\" The first practice open to everyone is Monday. Tickets are required and they're free. {"uri": "2024-07-431313276", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "20:04:51", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T20:04:51Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T20:00:23Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5411764979362488, "url": "https://eu.detroitnews.com/story/sports/nfl/lions/2024/07/23/detroit-lions-training-camp-preview-five-players-looking-to-have-bounce-back-years-in-2024/74511258007/", "title": "Lions training camp preview: Five players looking to have bounce-back years in 2024", "body": "Sports are often classified as a \"What have you done for me lately?\" kind of business, and there are plenty of Lions players with hype around their name after a successful 2023 season.\n\nBut inevitably, as one player grabs the brass ring of opportunity, another falls by the wayside. Perhaps it's for reasons out of their control, such as injuries, or maybe they were passed up on the depth chart by a player on his way to stardom. Maybe their play simply declined.\n\nAs veterans report to training camp, here are five Lions looking to have bounce-back years in 2024.\n\n\u25b6 John Cominsky, defensive lineman\n\nCominsky was a great story in the 2022 season. After being claimed off waivers from the Atlanta Falcons in May 2022 -- the Lions were one of eight teams to put a claim in, a fairly high number -- Cominsky made the most of his opportunity in a pivotal season for the franchise. He finished that season with 44 pressures, four sacks and 12 QB hits, earning himself a two-year contract to stay in Detroit.\n\nBut as the entire defensive line as a whole (outside of Aidan Hutchinson) took a step back in pass-rush success through the 2023 season, Cominsky was one of the players who couldn't quite return to form. His pressure totals dropped by 25% (to 33) despite seeing 434 pass-rush snaps, as opposed to 356 the previous season.\n\nAs we've mentioned throughout our training camp previews, there's hope the defensive line as a whole will see improvement through the hiring of vaunted position coach Terrell Williams. And with so much uncertainty in the unit entering camp, opportunity will be abound for Cominsky to stake his claim as a key contributor.\n\n\u25b6 James Mitchell, tight end\n\nMitchell was recovering from a torn ACL to begin his rookie season in 2022, and even with the arrival of Sam LaPorta, the Lions were hoping to see Mitchell continue that progress after a full, healthy offseason in 2023.\n\nBut despite showing some solid pass-catching ability the year prior -- he had 11 catches on 11 targets as a rookie -- Mitchell struggled to crack the rotation and saw just two targets last season. Lions general manager Brad Holmes is loyal to the players he drafted, so maybe this camp isn't quite as make-or-break as it seems from the outset. But with Shane Zylstra vying for the third tight end job, it feels as though Mitchell doesn't have much room for error.\n\n\u25b6 James Houston, outside linebacker\n\nHouston was one of the most exciting players to come out of the 2022 season, as the sixth-round rookie made his debut in Week 12 and went on to accumulate eight sacks in the final seven games. Many thought he was on a trajectory to be one of the defense's most impactful players last season.\n\nBut even before a broken ankle in Week 2 ended his season prematurely, there was reason to be skeptical about whether the Lions felt the same way about his potential as local and national media did. He mainly repped with the third team in practice as Detroit attempted to round out his abilities into somebody who could rush the passer and play off-ball linebacker, an area where he never really stood out.\n\nIn addition to seeing how he returns to this year's training camp, there's intrigue in seeing how the Lions plan to use Houston in Year 3.\n\n\u25b6 Donovan Peoples-Jones, wide receiver\n\nThrough each of the first three years of his career, Peoples-Jones saw vast improvements in production. But this past season, he wasn't quite in the mix with Cleveland, and after a midseason trade to Detroit, he turned in his quietest season as a pro: 13 receptions on 25 targets for a grand total of 155 yards and no touchdowns.\n\nPeoples-Jones' potential is obvious, and it makes sense why the Lions didn't feel compelled to force him into action with an offense that was absolutely humming. It can be difficult -- especially in an offense that depends on timing -- to get on the same page on the fly.\n\nBut even if we assume that Jameson Williams successfully takes a third-year jump, there should be plenty of opportunity for Peoples-Jones to bring something unique to the table as a big-bodied outside receiver with good hands.\n\n\u25b6 Emmanuel Moseley, cornerback\n\nWith all of the new talent in Detroit's secondary, it's easy to forget how intriguing the addition of Moseley was entering last season. Though he would be getting a late start due the rehab of his torn ACL, he had shown through his first five games of the 2022 campaign that he had become a surefire starting corner in the league.\n\nAfter finally being cleared to play, Moseley's season once again ended in a hurry, as he tore the opposite ACL on his second play back. But while he had the same road to recovery ahead of him as the year prior, it appears that things have gone a bit better this time. Moseley was not named as one of the players who would be starting training camp on the active/PUP list.\n\nWho knows how long it'll take Moseley to return to his best football after missing the better part of two full seasons, but he certainly can't be forgotten as the Lions aim to reshape their secondary once again.", "source": {"uri": "detroitnews.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "The Detroit {"uri": "2024-07-431359019", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-23", "time": "21:13:52", "dateTime": "2024-07-23T21:13:52Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-23T21:00:58Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5372549295425415, "url": "https://clutchpoints.com/1-surprising-player-who-could-make-or-break-lions-2024-nfl-season", "title": "1 surprising player who could make or break Lions' 2024 NFL season", "body": "If the Lions can find another consistent pass rusher to pair with Aidan Hutchinson, their defense will become a lot better.\n\nThe Detroit Lions are riding high after one of the most successful seasons in their franchise's history. Detroit came so close to the Super Bowl that they could taste it. Now, they are ready to attack the 2024 season with renewed vigor.\n\nThey got the 2024 NFL season off to a great start during the offseason. General manager Brad Holmes aggressively addressed the team's biggest need -- the defensive secondary. The Lions added Amik Robertson in free agency and traded for Carlton Davis III from the Buccaneers. They also invested their first two draft picks in cornerbacks, adding Terrion Arnold and Ennis Rakestraw Jr. These players join a secondary that already includes second-year standout Brian Branch and ball hawking free safety Kerby Joseph.\n\nHowever, there is one important position group that the Lions hardly addressed in either free agency or the 2024 NFL Draft. The Lions desperately need a reliable pass rusher to pair with Aidan Hutchinson.\n\nYou can say they haven't tried to find a solution. During free agency, the Lions signed journeyman Marcus Davenport to a one-year contract. Davenport comes with first-round pedigree, but injuries have hampered his NFL career. He is a cheap upside play, but not someone who the Lions should single-handedly depend upon for production.\n\nDetroit also has a handful of rotational role players who have made up the bulk of the team's pass rush the past few years. Josh Pascal and John Cominsky are both tweener players who can line up at edge rusher or kick inside for some interior pass rush. They will also try out CFL superstar Mathieu Betts, who has some Aidan Hutchinson vibes himself. These are all valuable players, but none of them have the realistic upside of becoming an every-down starter in 2024.\n\nFinally, there's James Houston. He may be more of a situational player, but he has the potential to become the team's best pass rusher this season.\n\nWho is James Houston?\n\nJames Houston was a relatively unheralded player in college who became a diamond in the rough for the Lions.\n\nHouston was recruited by the University of Florida to play linebacker. Things didn't pan out with the Gators, so Houston transferred to Jackson State and played for head coach Deion Sanders. It was coach Sanders who saw Houston's potential as a pass rusher.\n\nAccording to Jeff Risdon of Lions Wire, Houston pitched himself to Sanders as an off-ball linebacker. However, Sanders was quick to guide Houston in the right direction.\n\nThe following quotes come from an episode of Coach Prime on YouTube, which aired in 2022.\n\n\"I know the talent that I have,\" Houston said. \"And y'all have put a cap on my talent, here. I know exactly what I can do.\"\n\nCoach Prime gave Houston a blunt response in return.\n\n\"James, let me tell you something,\" Sanders retorted. \"If you were able to do that, you would have done that, and you would have never came here. If you was that dude that you think you are at linebacker, you would have never been here.\"\n\nIt turns out that Coach Prime was right. In his final collegiate season, Houston racked up 16.5 sacks as an edge rusher. His ability to rush off the edge and play some off-ball linebacker made him a tempting prospect for the Lions, who picked him in the sixth round.\n\nCan James Houston provide consistent pass rush for the Lions opposite Aidan Hutchinson in 2024?\n\nHouston has proved that he has what it takes to succeed as an NFL pass rusher. However, he hasn't mastered the most important ability yet -- availability.\n\nHouston put himself on the map in 2022 when he logged a whopping eight sacks and one forced fumble in only seven games played. In fact, according to Pro Football Focus, Houston managed this production only 92 pass rush snaps. It should go without saying, but I'll spell it out for you -- this is absolutely absurd efficiency!\n\nThe problem is it only came in a handful of games.\n\nHouston's 2023 season was cut short after he suffered a pedal ankle fracture in Week 2 against the Seattle Seahawks. He underwent tightrope surgery, which ended his season.\n\nIf we're being optimistic, this injury gave Houston a chance to catch up on the mental side of the game. That's why Lions fans are optimistic that Houston can have a larger impact if he can return healthy in 2024.\n\nJames Houston has a chance to become a dangerous situational pass rusher for the Lions as long as he can stay healthy. If Detroit gets what they're hoping for from Houston, their defense will become all the more ferocious.", "source": {"uri": "clutchpoints.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "ClutchPoints"}, "authors": The first move in that effort was acquiring Carlton Davis from the Tampa Bay Buccaneers. They also got sixth-round picks this year and next in the deal, while sending a 2024 third-round pick to Tampa Bay.\n\nDavis, as a top-notch man coverage corner, appears to be an ideal fit for what Lions defensive coordinator Aaron Glenn wants to do. There are durability concerns, as he has missed four of more games in three straight seasons. His level of play has fallen some in line with that, after he was second in the league in pass breakups in both 2019 and 2020.\n\nDavis is in the final year of his contract, and a change of scenery is probably good for him. This, albeit with no football having been played yet, looks to be a good trade for both sides.\n\nIt's a practical requirement to grade trades immediately after they happen, and we certainly had a lofty one for the Davis trade from a Lions' angle. As training camps start around the league, Tony Catalina of Pro Football Network looked back at the offseason to grade the best and worst NFL trades.\n\nCatalina has the Lions' trade for Davis among his five worst offseason trades, with a grade of C+. It is clearly a grade of the Lions' side of the deal.\n\n\"The Lions are a good football team that was close to a Super Bowl appearance last season. So, it makes sense for them to attack what many view as a weak spot by adding veteran CB Carlton Davis.\n\n\"However, Davis has been an oft-injured player over the last few years, and 2023 wasn't his best statistical year.\"\n\n\"Maybe a change of scenery will do him good, but with Detroit's approach to free agency and the draft, they may have been better served giving a younger guy a shot at winning a job.\"\n\nDavis will turn 28 late in the coming season (Dec. 31), so any attempt to classify him as old is a reach. He's got experience, up to and including a Super Bowl ring, and the Lions needed someone with that kind of resume after things didn't quite work out in the rebuild of their cornerback depth chart the year before.\n\nDavis has to play in games and remove the Cameron Sutton on-field PTSD from the psyche of Lions' fans. So it's fair to be a little skeptical of him until that happens, if it happens. {"uri": "8238341714", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-22", "time": "21:04:57", "dateTime": "2024-07-22T21:04:57Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-22T21:04:20Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5333333611488342, "url": "https://sidelionreport.com/posts/lions-have-history-to-overcome-if-they-are-going-to-take-next-step-this-year", "title": "Lions have history to overcome if they're going to take next step this year", "body": "The Detroit Lions will have to overcome some tough history to take their next step this season.\n\nFor the first half of last year's NFC Championship Game, it looked like the Detroit Lions were headed for their first Super Bowl. No need to rehash how the second half went, but the dynamic has changed with the Lions now the proverbial \"hunted\" rather than the \"hunter.\"\n\nThis spring, head coach Dan Campbell noted the challenge heading into this season.\n\n\"I mentioned this last year and I'll say it again: It's going to take a lot more than it did last year to get to where we were,\" Campbell said. \"That's just the nature of how it goes. But we're going to be more than capable of doing that. Things got to go your way, but it does start with you. It starts with those players, starts with the coaches. We've got to put the work in.\"\n\nPutting in the work will not be an issue for the Lions, be it coaches or players. They are embracing the expectations around them, and they expect to deliver. But as they emerge from their own lackluster franchise history, there's a piece of conference history working against them.\n\nAs part of his training camp preview, Dave Birkett of the Detroit Free Press noted the history of recent NFC runner-ups the following season.\n\nNo NFC runner-up has gone on to win the Super Bowl the next season since the Green Bay Packers in 1996. The Packers lost to the Dallas Cowboys in the 1995 NFC title game, then they beat the Bill Parcells, Drew Bledsoe-led New England Patriots in Super Bowl XXXI after the 1996 season.\n\nBefore last year's 49ers, no NFC team that lost in the previous year's conference championship game had advanced to the Super Bowl since the 49ers also did it under Jim Harbaugh in 2012. Of the 10 NFC runners-up from 2012-2021, five failed to make the playoffs. Campbell was on the New Orleans Saints' coaching staff when they lost the NFC Championship Game in 2018 then lost their first playoff game in 2019.\n\nThis is the kind of thing that, should they be aware of it, will further motivate the Lions this season. But there's no denying nearly 30 years of NFC runner-ups failing to take the next step to win the Super Bowl the following year, with many not reaching the conference title game that following year.", After an offseason full of additions and hype, the organization has high hopes for 2024.\n\nAmong other reasons, the Lions have unprecedented continuity in a league full of turnover and changes. Detroit held onto both of its coordinators despite head coaching interest and signed three core players to contract extensions.\n\nAs a result, the Lions have much of the same core in place that made a run to the NFC Championship game last year. He explained at the end of practice that he had simply consumed the wrong thing for breakfast.\n\nThe Alabama product showed off his defining trait during an early team period. Jared Goff hit him on a deep pass, and the wideout looked fast on an efficient route to haul in the toss. Overall, he looked stronger and more explosive in his performance.\n\n\"He just looks more comfortable. He looks like he's done this before,\" Amon-Ra St. Brown said. \"He looks like he knows what to expect. He's not that young, rookie guy no more. He's been here for a few years. Every year he just gets more comfortable. I know I've been saying this every year, but I think he's gotten better every year and I think this year's gonna be huge for him. The Tennessee product underwent adjustments to his footwork in the spring in an effort to better acclimate to Ben Johnson's offensive scheme that is based around timing.\n\nOn Wednesday, his passes looked sharp. During 7-on-7 drills, he connected on a strike with Daurice Fountain toward the right sideline. His delivery looked quicker, and the ball jumped out of his hand. Later in the drill, he also hit on a crisp toss to Jalon Calhoun toward the left sideline.\n\nHooker attacked his craft in the break between OTAs and camp. Among other things, he spent time with former Lions backup Teddy Bridgewater working on various nuances of development.\n\n\"We just really worked on timing and really taking control of the huddle, which I did a pretty good job of today,\" Hooker said. \"Once I calmed down, I had some jitters the first reps in team today. Once I calmed down and got my rhythm, I felt good.\"\n\nHis timing on passes looked much improved, as evidenced by an efficient delivery to Kalif Raymond. Hooker will still have to compete for the backup job with Nate Sudfeld, who returns for his third season with the organization.\n\nSudfeld had a nice connection with Calhoun on a deep throw, splitting Steven Gilmore and Kindle Vildor in the process. At one point in practice, he burst through the line on three straight plays. Had the practice been with pads, all three plays would've caused problems for the offense.\n\nCoaches complete up-downs\n\nCampbell and defensive coordinator Aaron Glenn participated in the team's annual up-down ritual, completing the necessary 40 with the defensive unit at the start of Wednesday's practice.\n\nThis is a yearly tradition for the Lions, who utilize the drill as an initiation leading into the start of the season.\n\nAdditionally, members of the offense and defense were wearing the guardian caps that have become a staple of training camp. Worn atop the helmet, these are designed for protection and to limit head injuries.\n\nPost-practice work\n\nSt. Brown has set the standard for the receiver room with his post-practice work on the JUGS machine. Hauling in 202 passes each day, the USC product is relentless with his work.\n\nOn the first day of camp, several players got work in on the machine following the conclusion of practice. {"uri": "8241591242", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "16:11:18", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T16:11:18Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T16:10:43Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.4901960790157318, "url": "https://norfolkdailynews.com/select/sweigard-recognized-at-lions-club-international-convention/article_86e60fe8-49ce-11ef-9adc-df5edc9a7d2d.html", "title": "Sweigard recognized at Lions Club international convention", "body": "MELBOURNE, Australia -- Leon Sweigard recently received a prestigious Lions honor. It took a journey halfway around the world for the Norfolkan to receive it.\n\nSweigard and his wife, Kelly, attended the 106th Lions International Convention from June 21-25.\n\nLeon Sweigard, a Norfolk Lions Club member, was inaugurated at the First Vice District Governors/District Governors-Elect seminar during the four-day event. Sweigard was one of 750 district governors recognized at the event.\n\nAbout 11,000 people from 208 countries attended the convention from across the world.\n\n\"It's pretty awesome for the Lions Club to put on such an event internationally,\" Kelly Sweigard said.\n\nLeon Sweigard has been a member of the Norfolk chapter of the Lions Club for the past 26 years. He is in his sixth year serving in a leadership role.\n\nThe recognition of district governor was only the most recent honor Leon Sweigard has received. Earlier this year, he was a recipient of the Melvin Jones award. Jones founded the Lions organization in 1917.\n\nDuring the trip, the Sweigards attended several more convention events, interacted with other Lions from around the world and even learned more about the Australian culture.\n\nBefore arriving in Australia, Sweigard was one of 14 Lions members from Nebraska attending the convention.\n\n\"When we went there, we had a lot of familiar faces,\" Leon Sweigard said. \"All of the sudden, you are in a different country halfway across the world, but you are with a group of people that made it very relaxing.\"\n\nInteracting with other Lions Club members from throughout the world was interesting for the Sweigards. At the beginning of the convention, they were presented with a translation box.\n\nThe Sweigards met the newly installed international president, Fabricio Oliveira of Brazil.\n\n\"If there was an international speaker who didn't speak your language, you had a setting to hear it in your language,\" Kelly Sweigard said. \"We had an opportunity to speak with a gentleman from France, and we used our phones to interact. Everybody was willing to do it. It was just neat that they want to converse with you and will use the tools to do it.\"\n\nSweigard and his wife went to a sanctuary 31 miles outside of Melbourne. There, they could see the koala bears and kangaroos. They also got to see how Australians raise their own food and how the animals were fed.\n\nTheir agriculture consists primarily of Brussels sprouts, strawberries, cherries and apple orchards.\n\n\"Their apple orchards are netted from top-to-side because they don't want blemishes on the food because it lowers the price,\" Leon Sweigard said. \"That's why they put netting over the apple orchards to stop the animals and the hail.\"\n\nThe kangaroo population is similar to the deer population in the United States.\n\nDay three of the convention featured a parade. The event was held on a 56-degree day in the heart of winter. Notable losses are located in the upper left-hand corner. Click on the picture to expand for a better look.\n\nWhat is HAVOC? I wanted to create a metric that better understood how defenders play within their scheme. For the D-line and LBs, it is pretty straightforward. Can you fit the run and create a pass rush? For LBs and some Edges, coverages have also been added.\n\nRelated Content: Field Vision Sports - Introducing Havoc Ratings\n\nIn the secondary, it can get complicated. Not every team runs the same amount of coverage. Some, like Dan Quinn, Jim Schwartz, and Gus Bradley, live in a singular style of play, while others, namely Mike Macdonald and Vic Fangio, choose to play a multitude of coverages. I wanted to create a more nuanced way to look at DB play. How are they playing within man and zone schemes, and how diverse is their coverage palate?\n\nUtilizing HAVOC, which is biased towards player and scheme usage, we can better understand how these players are used within the ecosystem they play in. A great example is Seattle's Riq Woolen, one of the best man coverage CBs in the game but struggles at zone. Team-wise, the Browns have three CBs that excel at man coverage, which suits what DC Schwartz is trying to do.\n\nHAVOC allows us to track free agency signings and paint a better picture of their fit. Should the Commanders, who will play mainly man and 3-match coverages, bring in a zone-centric CB? No, that wouldn't be wise. Using HAVOC allows us to see how teams are building their rosters defensively. So remember, these numbers show how productive the player was in the scheme they played in last year, which is reflected against their peers in their overall ranking.\n\nRelated Content: The Power of Evaluating Players using Play-by-Play Data\n\nThe ratings in this article are my 'raw' Havoc scores.
