Thanks to The Motley Fool, you can access the full story in this exclusive report.\n\n\" Unlock the secrets of tomorrow's tech revolution now.\n\nThe Lions shocked everyone the first week of last season when they came out and beat the Chiefs at home. From that point forward, Detroit had put everyone on notice. Fast-forward to the end of the season, and the Lions were NFC North divisional champs and headed to the playoffs, even winning a playoff game. All things that had not happened since the early '90s.\n\nMost pundits focus on the offense, but Detroit's defense has quietly had a resurgence. The previous year ('22) was a disaster in the secondary, but embattled defensive coordinator Aaron Glenn made a few tweaks in playcalling to alleviate issues there. Adding Quarters to a Cover 1 dominant scheme was a boon for the Lions all year, and it gave Detriot more answers and a layered approach.\n\nThe scheme is Nickel-based (68%/4-2-5) and mainly closed-post in the secondary. When in Base (27%), Detroit is multiple, able to align in a 3-4 or 4-3 depending on the game plan, but typically their alignment looked like a traditional 3-4. Derrick Barnes (LB19) or DE John Cominsky (DL37) came in to create the Lions Base. Barnes could moonlight as an Edge. Besides production in the back end, the most significant difference from '22 to '23 was the emergence of a Quarters scheme.\n\nThe '22 season saw the Lions sit atop the Cover 1 usage leaderboard at 30% of its calls. Detroit complemented that with Cover 3 at a similar rate. The secondary couldn't handle the heat.\n\nIn '23, Glenn came out against the Chiefs running Quarters on over 30% of their calls. Not every team got that treatment, though. The Vikings, for instance, only saw a few snaps of the coverage. Still, Glenn's ability to at least usher in change gave the Lions a much-needed boost on defense.\n\nOverall, the unit was still average in stopping the pass, so this offseason, the Lions went out and got Buccanners' CB Carlton Davis III (CB36) and drafted CB Terrion Arnold of Alabama. Both CBs excel in man coverage and have the coverage diversity to play Quarters. Glenn still wants to play man coverage but needs the CBs to do it.\n\nLast year, Detroit had the highest DVOA against the rush, yet still went out and got DJ Reader (DL34). The Lions are also banking on former Vikings first-round pick Marcus Davenport to have a bounce-back year after an injury cut his '23 season short. Glenn wants to live in 'sub' packages that feature man and man-match coverages, and several big splash off-season moves illustrate that philosophy. There are no more excuses for Glenn.\n\nSay what you want about Aidan Hutchinson (ED2), but the kid can rush the passer. He still needs to develop against the run to make him more of a complete player. Most of his production has come without much help from the opposite Edge. The hope is that Davenport or James Houston (or a combination of both) can give Hutchinson support.\n\nInside, the team signed DJ Reader, arguably one of the best Noses in the league. Alim McNeal (DL32) was productive last year at the 3 technique. DE Cominsky is a workhorse and will come in when the Lions want to run a 3-4 or Penny (5-1) package as the 3 tech. opposite McNeal. He can also play the 'big' 5 tech. in certain four-down packages.\n\nThe run-stopping ability of the Lions should continue with this group. More importantly, the Edge opposite of Hutchinson has to start showing up. Most teams will want to double Reader, allowing the other D-linemen to work their one-on-ones.\n\nThe Lions finished fifth in pressure rate but were 24th in average time to pressure. Reader should give the Edges better looks, and Detriot desperately needs Davenport or Houston to start playing ball opposite Hutchinson. It's not enough to stop the run in the modern NFL.\n\nAlex Anzalone (LB12) has quietly become one of the better LBs in the NFL. The Lions use him in various ways, and he is the solo backer in the team's Penny package (5-1). As a Will, or $-backer, he is mainly tasked with blitzing or defending the RB. His ability to stop the run is a bonus.\n\nJack Campbell (LB68) was drafted to be a traditional Mike or box LB; for the most part, he didn't disappoint. Campbell can hold down the box while Anzalone is used as a chess piece to create pressure of mismatches. The coverage aspect of Campbell will need to take another step this year to bring Detroit's defense into the top 10.\n\nLast year young Safety duo of Kerby Joseph (S50) and Ifeatu Melifonwu (S16). Melifonwu, in particular, had a knack for making plays as a pass rusher and the added value of being able to defend TEs when needed. Joseph has the potential to continue to grow in this system. Both need to become more competent in man coverage, but in true Lions fashion, they are both solid against the run.\n\nThe CB room will look completely different from the '23 version. Both starters, Jerry Jacobs (CB 72) and Cameron Sutton (CB59) are gone. The Lions traded for Buccaneers' CB Carlton Davis to replace them and drafted Terrion Arnold. Both CBs are man-coverage defenders and can play Quarters and Cover 3. Look at the CB spot if you want to see where Glenn and the Lions' brass heads are.\n\nFinally, the Lions have arguably the best Slot defender in all of football. Brian Branch instantly upgraded the defense and gave Detroit an every-down defender in one of the most critical positions in modern football. The rookie finished near the top of the DB charts in tackles for loss (TFLs) and second in picks by a rookie.\n\nGive it to Detroit for understanding that they need to solidify the secondary to win a championship. If Arnold can produce and Joseph continues to grow alongside Melifonwu, the secondary has the potential to take a significant leap.\n\nUnique Insights for Professionals, Proven predictions for fans. Football's Premier Predictive Analytics Platform. Click the logo to go directly to the site. And follow along on Twitter/X.\n\nThe Buccaneers under Todd Bowles seem to be treading water. Several pieces on defense are standouts, but they are potholed with players that seem not to be able to get over the hump. Tampa runs a 3-4 multiple defense that traditionally has run a lot of Cover 1.\n\nOver the past few seasons, Bowles has maintained his pressure-heavy scheme but has shifted his coverage palette to be more diverse, mainly playing zones. Up front, the team can easily transition from their base 3-4 into Nickel (4-2-5) with ease because of their two inside LBs and tough interior D-line.\n\nThat might not be the case this year, as longtime LB Devin White (LB34) will depart for greener pastures in Philly. The duo of White and Lavonate David (LB6) has always been one of the best in the NFL. The transition away from White shows how the NFL economy has shifted away from LBs as a priority in free agency.\n\nOne of the most significant additions to this year's team will be Jets Safety Jordan Whitehead (S26), whom the Bucs let walk several seasons ago. Once he hit the market this offseason, Tampa brought him back to work. Antoine Winfield Jr. (S2), who was an All-Pro last year, has quickly become one of the best Safety in the league. Pairing him with Whitehead gives the Bucs a dynamic backend.\n\nBowles has shown a knack for evolving his scheme to fit the needs of those on the roster. Last year, Tampa was second in the NFL in blitz rate, right behind the Vikings. The transition to zone is on par with others around the league. Bowles is banking on some personnel changes to bolster the defense and get it back into the top 10.\n\nInside is where the Buccaneers have the potential to be truly special. Nose Vita Vea (DL14) is a freak and, when healthy, is a one-of-one player. Last year's 1st-round draft pick, Calijah Kancey (DL27), showed flashes of greatness. The combination of Vea and Klancey gives the Bucs flexibility to hop from 3-4 to Ni without losing much production. DE Logan Hall (DL90) needs to begin showing up in production, though, or he could potentially see his way out the door.\n\nAt Edge, rookie Chris Braswell will be inserted into the fray to provide juice. Tampa lost Shaq Barrett (ED33) but hopes the addition of the Bama star can push players like Joe Tryon-Shoyinka (ED63) to begin playing up to their draft slot. Tryon-Shoyinka has shown sparks, but the Buccaneers opted not to take his 5th Year Option. He will be playing for his contract this fall.\n\nYaya Diaby (ED91) is in the same situation as JTS. The pressure is on for the young Edges. Tampa signed Randy Gregory (ED84) to provide depth, but he is currently AWOL from camp. If there is one group in the Tampa defense that has major question marks, it is the Edge group. Braswell has a clean slate and ample opportunity to earn a starting job before the season begins.\n\nGone is White, but David is still there to hold down the second level of the defense. A complete LB, David will create pressure if the Edges aren't up for the job. The Bucs blitzed so much last year because of the lack of pressure from outside.\n\nOpposite David will be KJ Britt (LB42), who shadowed White last year. The Tampa front office felt that he played well enough that the team could move on from White. Britt is good in the box and should allow Bowles to use David as a chess piece, moving him around to create mismatches or pressure.\n\nTo start the 2024 season, the Buccaneers might have the best Safety duo in football. The combination of Winfield and Whitehead is back, and both excel in zone schemes. The duo's pressure will be on to help keep a cap on the secondary, as the CBs are more of a question mark.\n\nWinfield was an elite do-everything workhorse as a pass rusher and one of the best run-stopping safeties in '23. He also dominated Cover 1 and Cover 3, which are the preferred coverages of Bowles.\n\nWhitehead will bring another dimension back into the secondary. A hybrid safety, Whitehead can be used as a tool opposite Winfield, who has an extensive background as a Nickel defender. Together, the two can act as counterweights in Bowles' scheme.\n\nAfter Carlton Davis's departure to the Lions, the CB duo will be Jamel Dean (CB25) and Zyon McCollum (CB56). Behind those two, there is no form of production. Whereas the Edge group has question marks centered around the lack of production, the CB questions center on a lack of depth.\n\nDean and McCullum are serviceable CBs, but there is no depth if one is injured. The only depth provided this offseason was the drafting of Tyreke Smith as a Ni/Safety hybrid, not a CB. The podium in the press room got all big and bulky, looking like it had spent the offseason working out.\n\nCoach Dan Campbell stood behind it and for the first time in his life he actually looked small.\n\n\"This is a huge podium,\" he quipped.\n\nRemember, back in the day, when you could \"super-size\" a pop at McDonald's? That's what has happened here -- this podium has been super-sized (and splashed with the Meijer corporate logo).\n\nThen again, everything around this team has been super-sized -- starting with a mountain of hope and belief -- so why not the podium?\n\nMaybe it was fitting that Campbell looked smaller behind that podium.\n\nBecause something else has changed behind the scenes. There was a time when he had to be not just the face of the team, but the soul. He had to teach an entire roster about grit and attitude and culture, imposing himself on everything while gritting his teeth over mistakes and misalignments.\n\nBut this team has evolved to the next stage. It's now a player-driven team, which is the best kind.\n\n\"Yeah, look this is their team,\" Campbell said, while listing several key leaders. \"We set the standards a long time ago, but now as players, you guys control it. So if it's not up to your standards, well, it needs to be said and let's do it again: You guys control it. We shouldn't have to worry about that anymore. That's on them. That's what I want, that's what I expect.\"\n\nTHE GOALS: Priority No. 1 for Lions at start of training camp? Avoid complacency\n\nRarely did a ball hit the ground. Quarterback Jared Goff was particularly impressive and particularly efficient.\n\nEverybody was moving and hustling between drills. It was like a well-oiled machine.\n\nSo, I asked running back David Montgomery about it: \"Did this feel pretty crisp and clean?\"\n\nAnd in keeping with the theme, that comment is actually huge.\n\nMonstrous, really.\n\nIf you think this team will rest on its laurels, much less its appearance in the NFC championship game, you don't know Campbell.\n\nMore importantly, you don't understand how they have built this team.\n\n\"Your own worst enemy is yourself,\" Campbell said from behind that giant podium. \"It's not anybody else, it's really not the opponent, it's always going to be yourself. So, we're always going to have to guard against -- I'll bring it up again, the complacency, the entitlement, the reputation. Like, 'What is that? That's nothing. We've got to go back to work.' \"\n\nThey might not win as many games as last year -- you never know what will happen in any given season with injuries, crazy bounces, last-second drives or anything else that can go wrong in the NFL. (See: The last 60 years of the Lions franchise.)\n\nBut I seriously doubt it will be because of complacency.\n\n\"We don't live off reputation, we live off of work,\" Campbell said. \"And that's what's gotten us where we're at, it's been a long, hard road to get to where we're at right now, and there's a price to be paid, and so we've got to go pay it again. That's the message, and it'll always be the message.\"\n\nDAVE BIRKETT: With familiar faces everywhere, Lions at 'Level 401' entering training camp\n\nLions offensive coordinator Ben Johnson stopped everything.\n\nJohnson moved a wide receiver a few yards closer to the sideline, and it felt like a little thing that was actually a big thing.\n\nThose tiny details will determine everything.\n\n\"You should feel like we're ready to go play right now,\" Campbell said. \"Now, is it good enough? No, it won't be good enough, that's why we have camp. But yeah, man, it should -- from the outside looking in, like, 'Man, these guys could go play right now.' And that's what I expect.\"\n\nAfter the first practice was done, about 40 players stayed on the field, putting in extra work.\n\nIf nothing else, that is a reflection of everything that Campbell has infused into this team.\n\n\"We're not going to lose our identity,\" Campbell said. \"That is the most important thing to me, and I won't sacrifice it for anyone or anything. He started to Goff's right and made a beeline up the seam and angled for the opposite pylon, blowing past rookie Ennis Rakestraw and Ifeatu Melifonwu to get open for a bomb of a touchdown pass from Goff.\n\nOn his way back to the huddle, though, Williams puked and reportedly told MLive on his way off the field that he had eaten the wrong thing for breakfast. He wasn't involved much in the later portions of practice, which was generally a light day for many players; All-Pro Amon-Ra St. Brown, for example, only had one catch during the day.\n\n\u25b6 The limited practice production from St. Brown and Williams provided an opportunity for a few other players to shine. Undrafted rookie Jalon Calhoun made a pair of nice catches, including a deep ball over the middle from Nate Sudfeld that he caught over Steven Gilmore. Daurice Fountain, who was with the team's practice squad for much of last season, also made some noise, with a high-point catch from Hendon Hooker near the sideline being the highlight of his day.\n\n\u25b6 Hendon Hooker showed some positive developments during the spring portion of the offseason, but it was noticeable that he had some room to grow before the Lions could feel comfortable throwing him out there in a pinch. Wednesday, Hooker looked far more decisive than he did at any point during OTAs and minicamp.\n\nAfter scrambling under duress and sailing a pass to Kalif Raymond in the first set of team drills, Hooker settled down and was on the money for the rest of practice. He went 4-for-4 in the ensuing seven-on-seven drills, including a few difficult throws near the sideline and over the middle of the field. He extended that success into his next set of 11-on-11 work, going 3-for-3 with a variety of throws.\n\n\u25b6 While it's typical this time of year for the defense to be ahead of the offense, that was not the case Wednesday. The Lions' offense was firing on all cylinders; call it a benefit of bringing pretty much everybody (including offensive coordinator Ben Johnson) back from last season. In addition to Hooker's success, Goff started his day 3-for-3 and missed just one pass the rest of practice, firing incomplete to Raymond on an out route in his final set of 11-on-11. {"uri": "8241652648", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-24", "time": "16:55:44", "dateTime": "2024-07-24T16:55:44Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-24T16:55:02Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.4313725531101227, "url": "https://www.forbes.com/sites/stevesilverman/2024/07/24/lions-are-strong-no-1-in-dangerous-nfc-north-but-competition-abounds/", "title": "Lions Are Strong No. 1 In Dangerous NFC North, But Competition Abounds", "body": "The NFC North appears to have risen to the top of the heap in the NFL. All four teams have a chance to develop into winners in the 2024 season, and one of those teams could emerge as the NFC's Super Bowl representative at the season's conclusion.\n\nMake no mistake about it, there is definitely a pecking order and the Detroit Lions and Green Bay Packers have a clearer path than the Chicago Bears or Minnesota Vikings, but all four teams could have memorable seasons.\n\nEach team has strengths that could propel them to help them perform in a dynamic way. In this piece, we will identify the greatest strength that each of these teams has to offer.\n\nThe Lions know that it's what's up front that counts. Quarterback Jared Goff is a wonderful story who has risen to his greatest heights in Detroit, and Amon-Ra St. Brown has established himself as one of the toughest wideouts in the league. Tight end Sam LaPorta caught 86 passes in his rookie season and he has no limitations as he goes forward.\n\nBut no position group is stronger than the offensive line. Dan Campbell talked about his team's Super Bowl aspirations in the offseason, and that's because the Lions have a group of blockers who can just take over. Right tackle Penei Sewell was a first-team All-Pro last season and he may be the best blocker in the league. Frank Ragnow is nearly as good at center and was also an All-Pro. Left tackle Taylor Decker is just a notch or two below those two, and right guard Graham Glasgow is quite solid. The Lions added right guard Kevin Zeitler in the offseason, and the former Raven is one of the best pass blockers in the league.\n\nWhen the game is on the line in the fourth quarter, look for this group to take over.\n\nThere is no position group on the Packers that can match the Lions' excellence on the offensive line, but Jordan Love has a chance to become one of the game's elite quarterbacks. Is it unfair that the Packers have a QB progression of Brett Favre, Aaron Rodgers and now Love? That's a question for another day, even if Bears fans curse their fate as they consider this issue on an every-day basis.\n\nLove had a brilliant first year as the team's QB1. He completed 409 of 634 passes for 4,625 yards with a 98.5 passer rating along with 28 touchdown passes and 13 interceptions. As good as his regular season was, he was significantly better in the playoffs. He eviscerated the Dallas Cowboys by completing 16 of 21 passes for 272 yards and 3 touchdowns while keeping it clean on the interception side of the ledger.\n\nLove is expecting to get a contract extension from the Packers before the end of training camp, and he should get it. He is conducting a \"hold-in,\" and says he won't practice until he gets a new contract. While his sample size is not huge, his peak efforts are sensational and most expect him to get a deal that will put him in the neighborhood of Joe Burrow and Trevor Lawrence.\n\n\"He'll get paid,\" an agent told The Athletic. \"Love is young and has been in that building for several years. He showed that the playoff stage wasn't too big for him and never complained about sitting. I can't see why they wouldn't make him the highest-paid quarterback or close to it.\"\n\nLove carries the hopes and dreams of the Packers on his shoulders.\n\nThe Bears are banking on No. 1 draft choice Caleb Williams having a brilliant rookie season and leading the team out of the abyss the team has been in for years. That's a scary proposition because the adjustment to the NFL is rarely as smooth as C.J. Stroud made it look last year with the Houston Texans. It is usually much closer to the way 2023 No. 1 draft choice Bryce Young played with the Carolina Panthers last season.\n\nWhile Williams will have to answer questions, he does have a group of elite receivers waiting for him to develop. D.J. Moore is the holdover and he is coming off a brilliant 96-1,034-8 season that showed off his toughness as well as his all-around skill. Keenan Allen established himself as one of the best technical receivers during his run with the Los Angeles Chargers. Allen says rookie Rome Odunze is further ahead in his development than he was as a rookie. This is a group that can dominate on an every-week basis.\n\nThis brings us to the Vikings, and this team will have the biggest mountain to climb in order to play winning football. The questions are numerous with a placeholder quarterback in Sam Darnold and a rookie-in-waiting in J.J. McCarthy. Will running back Aaron Jones give the Vikings a lift at the running back slot? Can wideout Jordan Addison build off his impressive rookie season or will off-the-field issues continue to dog him?\n\nBut the Vikings have the best wideout in the league in Justin Jefferson and one of the best left tackles in Christian Darrisaw. Both men have been paid in the most elite fashion and are expected to dominate. Jefferson has shown he can make the biggest and most difficult catches under pressure, while Darrisaw shows off his balance and strength on an every-game basis.\n\nIt's a much bigger hill for the Bears and Vikings than the Lions and the Packers, but all four have a chance to do something special this season.", "source": {"uri": "forbes.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Forbes"}, "authors":
